 You mean the whole… Band-Aid thing.

Dr. Okorie:

 Yeah. We only picked up the artifacts because somebody wanted to maintain the status quo. These are miracle treatments.

Chief Ibanez:

 This place is beyond miracles.

<She turns back to the bay again, and points.>

Chief Ibanez:

 That's where the pier was. Crocker stood on the end.

.

Elizabeth Crocker, PoI-001, 

cryptomancer

 and Chaos Insurgency collaborator.

 And watched.

<She shifts her pointing angle slightly to the west.>

Chief Ibanez:

 There was a ship in port. The 

Northern Reach.

 It sank in the first big fight, and disappeared along with everything else after the last one.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 That's strange. Why would the ship disappear?

Chief Ibanez:

 Why would anything disappear?

<Chief Ibanez slides down the cliffside slightly, and gestures with her chin.>

Chief Ibanez:

 My sister and I treaded water just over there. Watched her watch us burn.

<She sighs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Always thought someday I'd be able to return the favour.

Dr. Okorie:

 Well, Crocker's still alive. Still 

at large

.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah, but she hasn't got anything worth burning. Takes the fun right out of it.

<She climbs back up, and begins walking again. Rather than taking the path further along the bay to the right, she turns left again and backtracks to the elbow of the table's arc.>

<She stops in front of a large, angular depression in the earth in front of the most prominent cleft in the surrounding cliffs.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What was here?

<Chief Ibanez attempts to respond, frowns, and clears her throat before attempting again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 My house. Our house.

<She walks to the edge of the depression, but this time does not step down into it. Her toe nudges the foliage, once, and then she steps back.>

Chief Ibanez:

 All the walls were at funny angles. Metal sheets riveted together. It was fine inside, but from outside it looked like a hovel. All the houses did.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Who built them?

<Chief Ibanez shrugs, and walks around the edge of the foundation's outline.>

Chief Ibanez:

 My grandfather's generation, I always figured. Based on the design of the metal. I did some reading…

<She grimaces, then reaches up to clutch her temple.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What's wrong?

Chief Ibanez:

 I gave myself a crash course on engineering in the facility that 

isn't

 over there anymore.

<She waves irritably in the direction of the distant beach.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Everything associated with it is associated with at least one memory the Foundation yanked out of my head when they picked me up. Anyway, that's how I know. How old the shacks were.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Was there anything older?

Chief Ibanez:

 What, you mean like, wood? Thatched cottages? Stone ruins? Nothing like that.

Dr. Okorie:

 A village without a past.

Chief Ibanez:

 Or future.

<Chief Ibanez looks over her shoulder, and pulls SCP-6500-SWORD out of its sheathe by a few inches. She squints, huffs, and releases it again.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 There's one more place we should check out, before we go on.

<Chief Ibanez walks around the imprint of her house and heads through the cleft, and the other two follow. The trees are thicker here, and although there is a path, it is faint and winding. The ground beneath their feet gradually rises.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Where are we going? I thought the whole village was on the coast.

Chief Ibanez:

 Most of it was. My grandfather lived further inland.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 How come?

Chief Ibanez:

 He didn't like people. I take after him.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What do you think you'll find there?

<Chief Ibanez shrugs, a sour look on her face.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Bad memories and scorched grass. Probably not very much of either, all these years later.

<There is a small clearing in the woods, where the rising ground briefly evens out. A few rotting timbers, and some preserved by combustion, are covered in vibrant ivies. The footprint of the shack cannot be easily discerned.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Del, what the hell is going on with the sword?

<SCP-6500-SWORD is now glowing serenely; the sheathe itself no longer fully blocks the transmission of its light.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Oh, figure it out already.

<She heads farther up the pass, which finally reaches the end of the natural cleft. It begins to switchback and wind as it traverses the cliffside, going up.>

<There is a landing several minutes and perhaps one hundred feet above the cleft floor. The cliff wall is broken by a yawning cave entrance. Chief Ibanez, breathing deeply, immediately crosses the threshold. The other two follow.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 How deep does this go?

Chief Ibanez:

 I never found out.

Dr. Okorie:

 We could get flashlights. Hell, I could 

make

 flashlights.

<She looks down at the rock floor, at a small black smudge.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Is this where…?

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah. This is where I hid out. We hid out. Yésica and me.

<Chief Ibanez blows out a breath.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Then just me.

<She walks to the mouth again, and points to a rocky outcropping out of sight from the cave proper.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I did my first dissection just over there.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Dissection?

Chief Ibanez:

 One thing dead people are really good at is teaching you how to make more dead people.

<She turns back to the cave, and the ash still visible on the floor.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Can't believe this is still here. Foundation must have crawled over every inch of this place. Didn't disturb the fire.

<She closes her eyes, stretches her muscles, and then in one fluid motion reaches over her shoulder with one hand to remove SCP-6500-SWORD from its sheathe.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 So much for the flashlights.

<The entire cave is immediately illuminated. SCP-6500-SWORD is glowing fiercely.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Did you know this was going to happen, Del?

Chief Ibanez:

 No. And I'm kind of pissed off that it worked, honestly.

<They blink in the brilliant light.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I guess there's more than one way to be a hero.

<Chief Ibanez walks to the cave mouth again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 This wasn't heroism. This was the easy part.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What's the hard part?

<Chief Ibanez responds over her shoulder.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Couple options. Depends what we see when I walk into the gulch with this thing in my hand.

<After a moment, the other two follow her.>

<The trio walk in silence for the next twenty minutes, descending the cliff face, following the cleft, and resuming their trek along the main bay path. They have reached the northernmost point of the table's arc before Dr. Okorie breaks the silence.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Did you want to talk about any of the rest of this?

Chief Ibanez:

 Nope.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I'm sure there's a lot of memories connected to—

Chief Ibanez:

 Sword's charged. Don't care.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 This is probably your last chance to come to peace with what happened here.

Chief Ibanez:

 I don't come to 

peace.

<Chief Ibanez brandishes SCP-6500-SWORD at her.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Boy, is that thing getting bright.

Chief Ibanez:

 Uh-huh.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What happens if it gets too charged?

Chief Ibanez:

 It doesn't.

Dr. Okorie:

 It bleeds its energy out into the environment at all times. Stirring up whatever needs stirring.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What if nothing needs stirring?

Dr. Okorie:

 Apparently, nothing never does.

<It takes a further forty-seven minutes to complete the circuit of the bay. Chief Ibanez pauses twice more; once at a large, roughly rectangular depression scarred by ash, and once at a large circular one on the edge of the bay cliffs. Both times she declines to comment.>

<The trio reach the beach. Chief Ibanez walks to the water's edge, removes a pair of collapsible binoculars from her belt and watches the distant helicopter across the bay. Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie engage in brief, hushed conversation.>

<Support personnel from Delta-6500 complete the circuit as well, and begin setting up equipment on the beach. Chief Ibanez shrugs the holster and sheathe off her shoulders, hands her service weapon to a nearby operator, hefts SCP-6500-SWORD, and heads for a wide break in the cliffs to the north. Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie follow.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You think this is going to work?

Chief Ibanez:

 No.

Dr. Okorie:

 If it doesn't, I can try manipulating the granules. See if there's anything residual in the…

<She winces as SCP-6500-SWORD flares. The narrow cliff walls to either side of them reflect the light, glowing bright white.>

<It takes just over eleven minutes to walk the overgrown route from the beach to a widening of the path, dotted with foliage and fallen stones, where the gulch ends in a sheer rock face.>

<Chief Ibanez walks to the centre of the clearing, raises SCP-6500-SWORD over her head, and holds it there.>

<SCP-6500-SWORD emits a pulse of light, and then another. Each pulse strikes the surrounding rocks, and they begin to vibrate. A hollow ringing sound fills the air, and then a grinding groan.>

Chief Ibanez employing SCP-6500-SWORD.

<An angular outline begins to form on the rock face at the rear of the canyon. As SCP-6500-SWORD continues to pulse, details become visible: concrete detailed to resemble stone, a wide lintel, and a set of broad, steel sliding doors.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Jesus Christ.

<The pulses from SCP-6500-SWORD weaken, then taper off entirely. The blade's glow is now very weak. Chief Ibanez lowers it again, and draws a deep breath.>

<The missing facility is now present. It shows no sign of wavering again.>

Dr. Okorie:

 The sword abhors a vacuum.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Change begets change.

Chief Ibanez:

 Trauma is a conga line.

<She waits for her equipment to be returned, then gestures at the door.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Let's go.

<The facility's front doors open when they draw near. They enter into a clean, spacious airlock; the interior doors do not open immediately, and the trio pause before approaching them.>

<The words INSTITUTO de CONTENCIÒN SEGURA are printed in bold letters over the lintel.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Instituto de Contenciòn Segura?

Chief Ibanez:

 It means—

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Obviously I know what it means. But, I mean, how?

Dr. Okorie:

 Could be a precursor. One of the groups that came together to form the Foundation.

Chief Ibanez:

 Lot of them were real disorganized. Bad record keeping. Some, we're still picking up the pieces decades later. 

Lost outposts

, rogue security systems still plugging away with nobody to defend.

Dr. Okorie:

 Right. So it must be that.

Chief Ibanez:

 Except it also 

can't

 be.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Because of the suit?

Chief Ibanez:

 Because of the suit.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Alternate reality, then.

Dr. Okorie:

 Which makes a certain sense.

Chief Ibanez:

 A certain nonsense.

Dr. Okorie:

 What do you mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 You were going to say it makes a certain sense that this thing is from an alternate dimension, because so are your people, and you think your people and my people are 

our

 people.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Should I know what you guys are talking about?

Dr. Okorie:

 I don't think of the people you're calling my people 

as

 my people, Del but other than that, yes. That's right.

Chief Ibanez:

 Only they were all from the same alternate dimension, and they had their big break up in this one. So where does a dimension-hopping Foundation precursor facility fit into that?

<Dr. Okorie shrugs.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Only one way to find out.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It always feels like telling on ourselves when we say that.

<Chief Ibanez returns to the exterior doors. They slide open to reveal four members of Delta-6500 in tactical gear, standing at attention.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Guess we should have brought Hammer Down, but that's hindsight, and today's subject is 

foresight.

 So, eyes forward. Look, but don't touch.

<The seven members of Delta-6500 approach the interior doors, Chief Ibanez leading.>

<The doors close.>

<Chief Ibanez walks through the open doors.>

<The doors open.>

<The agents pause on the far side of the doors.>

<The doors close.>

<The agents walk through the open doors.>

<The hall beyond is an infinitely fractalized series of airlocks.>

<The agents exit the facility, backward.>

<The hall beyond is a clean, white-tiled corridor. The floor is the ceiling.>

<The agents walk through the open ceiling.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Oh no.

<The agents walk through the closed ceiling.>

Dr. Okorie:

 It's like the Breach.

Chief Ibanez:

 It wasn't like this when I left. Pretty sure.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You left a long time ago.

Chief Ibanez:

 Or maybe just yesterday. Alright folks, SCRAMBLE and Scranton. And let's get a wire going.

<Delta-6500 are fitted with SCRAMBLE helmets, personal reality anchors and a double-reinforced tether line before proceeding further.>

<As they walk down the halls, brief fluctuations in reality occur before the roaming stabilization fields assert baseline again. Agents occasionally appear to be moving backward, or covering the same ground multiple times, or on one occasion, progressing at an impossible angle relative to the floor. Surrounding signage is all in Spanish, heavily distorted. They pass windowed laboratories, sitting nooks, and at least one vending machine. Everything is in a very poor state of repair, as though abandoned for decades after many more decades of hard use.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I feel like I'm going to run into myself in here.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 But which version of you?

Dr. Okorie:

 There's only ever one version of you.

Chief Ibanez:

 Beg to differ.

<Further progress is stalled when Delta-6500 turn a corner and discover that the hall beyond has been replaced by a bright orange swamp illuminated with fist-sized fireflies. The door to an office supposedly belonging to one Dr. Alvarez is framed by a pair of oak trees, pulsating with light.>

<Chief Ibanez tentatively taps the surface of the water with her boot. The clear ringing of porcelain tile can be heard.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Okay, so. This is bullshit—

Dr. Okorie:

 Who's that?

<Chief Ibanez draws her service weapon. The other Mobile Task Force members follow suit.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I don't see anybody.

Agent Koslova:

 I was just surprised that Dr. Okorie didn't.

Dr. Okorie:

 It's just us, Del. Or did you hear something?

Chief Ibanez:

 I was talking to Udo.

Chief Ibanez:

 Or the White Rabbits.

Agent Koslova:

 Yeah, alright. Sorry.

Dr. Okorie:

 I don't have the entire list memorized.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Who are you talking to?

Agent Koslova:

 Obviously 

I

 know that.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 They handle temporal and spatial anomalies.

Agent Koslova:

 The Angle Grinders?

Dr. Okorie:

 I'm right here.

Chief Ibanez:

 I think we need to get the Angle Grinders in here.

<Chief Ibanez raises SCP-6500-1 over her head. A faint glow surrounds the task force members, and time becomes linear again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Follow me. And zip it.

<Delta-6500 exit the facility. Reality failures and chronological dilation begin to plague them again as they reach the airlock; SCP-6500-SWORD is no longer glowing at all, and Chief Ibanez sheaths it before kicking the nearest wall in frustration.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Did you experience anything like that before?

Chief Ibanez:

 I think there was something wonky with time, but it can't have been that bad. I got shit 

done

 in there.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Holy…

<She is staring at Chief Ibanez's back. Chief Ibanez turns to face her.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

<Dr. Astrauskas walks around Chief Ibanez.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 The aura.

<Chief Ibanez turns in place, trying to face Dr. Astrauskas again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 If you're about to tell me I'm emotionally agitated—

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Not 

your

 aura. I couldn't see it before, because of the glow. I'm talking about the 

sword's

 aura.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why does the sword have an aura?

Dr. Okorie:

 Maybe it's alive?

<Chief Ibanez glares over her shoulder at the pommel of SCP-6500-SWORD.>

Chief Ibanez:

 No. I hate that. No.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 More likely it's literally absorbing something from you.

Dr. Okorie:

 What kind of something? The stuff we already knew about?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Maybe? I feel like I haven't seen protagonistic potentiality turn up in an aura before. And plenty of our co-workers are plenty dynamic.

Chief Ibanez:

 One more question for the pile. And I think I know how to get them all answered at once.

<Chief Ibanez sighs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I really do hate stories, though.

<Transcript ends.>

Addendum 8273-8, Exploration (Facility):

 After emerging from the structure — identified internally as Facility-34 — Delta-6500 camped on the Zevalan beach for the night. Due to the high priority of Protocol GYRUS, both MTF Theta-90 ("Angle Grinders") and MTF Lambda-5 ("White Rabbits") were transported to the site by daybreak; Chief Ibanez requested an additional consult, who would arrive the following day. Installation of full-scale Scranton Reality Anchors required several hours of work; by midmorning the Facility was sufficiently restored to baseline that exploration could continue while the remainder was secured.

Chief Ibanez, Dr. Astrauskas and Dr. Okorie each led investigation teams into the Facility interior to determine its contents, meeting back at the entrance hall shortly before noon.

Instituto de Contenciòn Segura emblem, Facility-34.

<Transcript begins.>

<Dr. Okorie is sitting in a red plastic visitor's chair against a dusty, tiled wall. The insignia of the Secure Containment Institute is visible, though faded, on the tiles. Chief Ibanez is pacing; she is wearing an old Foundation-issue bomber jacket, circa 1990s, over her jumpsuit. She did not bring it with her to Caleta San Roque.

>

<Dr. Astrauskas arrives, clipboard in hand. She waves the clipboard at the other two.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Just got a report from the radiologists.

<Chief Ibanez stops pacing.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah? Anything interesting?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Only that this building is about six hundred years old.

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Yeah.

Chief Ibanez:

 No, 

what?

 That's not just weird. That's fucking impossible.

Dr. Okorie:

 All I've got is weird, unfortunately.

Chief Ibanez:

 Well?

Dr. Okorie:

 Hydroponics. Weird hydroponics. And what looks like a bunch of old demonics circuitry, shorted out.

<Dr. Astrauskas sits in the chair beside Dr. Okorie's.>

Dr. Okorie:

 I took a look at the climate controls. The reason it was just a bunch of dirt is that all the plants died. The reason all the plants died?

Chief Ibanez:

 Don't leave me in suspense.

Dr. Okorie:

 They got too warm.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 As in, they scorched? Dehydrated?

Dr. Okorie:

 As in they got warm. Room temperature.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Okorie:

 This Facility has what's got to be the world's only hydroponic freezer.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 So… you're saying they were growing Stranger-in-the-Mist.

<Chief Ibanez shakes her head.>

Chief Ibanez:

 That doesn't make any sense. We traded for that with Puerto Extraño.

Dr. Okorie:

 I don't think it was a very healthy crop. They probably needed to refresh it a lot with plants from outside.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What would they have been doing with the flowers at all, though? On an industrial scale?

Chief Ibanez:

 Visions in bulk? I don't know.

Dr. Okorie:

 What did you find, Del?

Chief Ibanez:

 A big machine that doesn't work anymore. And the armoury.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Any of those fancy suits still in there?

<Chief Ibanez nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 They're all in locked cases. Directorial override. I found the keycard while I was scrounging, and I hid it. Hid it real well.

<She produces said keycard. There is no name or photograph, only security clearance and position information.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Well, that's definitely a win. What else did you have socked away in here?

Chief Ibanez:

 My journal.

<She tosses an antiquated personal tape recording device into Dr. Okorie's lap.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You knew where to find it.

Chief Ibanez:

 I did.

Dr. Okorie:

 Did you know before you came back in here?

Chief Ibanez:

 I did not.

<Dr. Okorie rewinds the tape, and presses the 'Play' button.>

<The voice is that of Chief Ibanez, roughly as she sounded after pickup by the Foundation in 1994.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 They're all dead.

<Silence on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 

Remember that

. They're all 

dead

.

<Silence on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 I can't fix that. But I can do something about it.

<Click on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 I don't understand this place at all.

I can read a lot of their files. The older stuff is mostly in Spanish. The newer stuff is usually English. Somebody took a marker to the oldest stuff, and it's a really magic marker because I'm pretty sure there's nothing underneath anymore. It's technical and blunt. The new stuff is looser. Sometimes handwritten.

I almost think I recognize the handwriting.

But what's this place even for? The files don't make sense. It sounds like outsiders came here to watch us, but then ended up giving us the keys to this place and… what? Going away? Why would they do that?

There's a lot of references to a machine in the lower levels. I don't know what it's for. Maybe it can help me.

Maybe it's a bomb.

<Click on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 It's not a bomb.

<She sighs.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 I read some notes. There's supposed to be an operator's manual, but I can't find that. All I can find is what somebody wrote down about what was in it, and that doesn't tell me what the thing actually 

does,

 just how to make it do it. I switched it on. Nothing exploded. That was disappointing.

There's a startup sequence. I don't really think I understand it. Feels like I need to know a lot more before I can make this thing work.

There's a lot of books in here. A lot of stuff on tape, and files on the computers. I'm going to do some reading.

It's not like there's any rush.

They're all dead.

And nobody is coming for me.

<Chief Ibanez walks away, back down the hall.>

<Dr. Okorie pauses the recording.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Do you want us to—

Chief Ibanez:

 No need.

<She tenses her shoulders as she walks.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I remember it all, now.

<Dr. Okorie resumes the recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 I don't know how long I've been reading. But I noticed something strange today.

I… haven't been eating.

At all.

I haven't used the outhouses. Haven't had a drink of water.

I took a look at the camera, the exterior camera.

At first I thought it was a coincidence. It was evening, just like the first time I looked. But no.

Crocker is still out there. Still waiting for my answer.

Still standing next to my brother's…

<Silence on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 I don't think time passes in here. Not until I look through that camera.

Maybe it's like that experiment with the cat. I don't know.

But it's giving me ideas.

I've got enough science equipment in here to run experiments of my own.

<Click on recording.>

<Chief Ibanez is now standing at the end of the hall, her back to Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 It's been three months. I've spent almost the whole time tearing everything out of the walls, looking for keycards and hidden doors.

Found some.

I found their training materials. I found their hospital. I found the gym, and the vitamins and supplements. I've been listening to engineering books on tape while I tear my muscles over and over again.

I think I'd clean up at the Olympics.

I know how the machine works now. At least, I think I know. I'm going to try and turn it on.

Maybe it doesn't do anything useful.

That doesn't really matter. I came in here looking for a weapon, and I found one.

<Click on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 I spent this afternoon outside. Outside the Facility.

Outside 

everything.

I fired up the machine, fed in the flowers, just like it said. I keyed in the first sequence I found in the back of the manual, and I hit the big red button.

Pretty light show. I threw up.

I checked the exterior camera.

Pitch black.

I waited twenty minutes, and when I didn't see anything else, I went to the front door and opened it.

There really wasn't anything out there.

Anything at all.

I almost expected to suffocate, but the air didn't exchange. I could breathe out there just as well as I can breathe in here.

I came back in eventually, when I got tired of staring at nothing. Reversed the sequence, hit the button.

I'm here again.

She's still out there.

I'm going to go through every sequence in the book.

<Click on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 It was just like home. Only empty, and greener.

I swam in a bay filled with algae and fish I could see through.

I ate one of the fish for dinner. Caught it with my bare hands, and barbecued it at the front door. I don't think it had ever seen a predator before.

It's going to be just like that, when I come back. For the last time.

<Click on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 When I spend too long outside, something funny happens in my head.

The stuff I did, I don't remember. I don't remember what I was doing in here, when I'm out there. I don't remember what I did out there, when I get back in here.

The stuff I learn, that sticks. But I can't picture how I learned it. I've got callouses on my hands, and I don't know how I got them.

I wish my other memories worked the same way.

<Click on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 Half of the sequences lead nowhere. The rest lead to places that are… waiting. Waiting to become somewhere.

They're all shaped like the Cala. Like Zevala, without the village. And they're all different. Sometimes a little. Sometimes a lot.

Two days ago I went rock climbing in a big, grey, crumbling canyon with a dark red sky overhead.

Yesterday I ran a marathon in a white salt desert.

Today was endurance testing in what looked like nuclear winter. It was so cold.

I don't know where I'm going tomorrow.

I think the machine's starting to sound strange. Stranger than before. Like maybe something's wrong.

I think I understand the repair instructions, but they want a lot of stuff I haven't got. Or maybe I do have it, and I just haven't found the right storage room yet.

Probably not worth chancing.

I found a suit of armour in the security lockup. I've been practicing with it.

I know what I'm going to do.

And when it's done, I'll come back in here, and keep running the sequences.

Maybe I'll try a few of my own.

Maybe I'll fix the machine before I do that.

Maybe I won't.

<Click on recording.>

Ibanez (Recording):

 I'm ready.

The machine caught fire when I got back. I used up a whole fire extinguisher making it stop. It still turns on, but the lights are all red.

I went into the freezer. Couldn't see my breath anymore. Red lights there, too.

End of the line.

I left the monitor on all day. Crocker lasted a few hours, then dragged my brother's body off camera. I can see the shadow of movement at the end of the canyon. I know they're still out there. They think they can wait me out.

They think they've got time.

<She laughs. The tone is flat.>

Their time is up.

<The tape stops.>

<Chief Ibanez returns to Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie. The latter is still holding the recording device, and staring at it in shock. Dr. Astrauskas attempts to speak, but Chief Ibanez cuts her off with a curt gesture.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Roz, did you find anything else?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 No… Del, this tape—

Chief Ibanez:

 We'll get to that. Focus up.

<Dr. Astrauskas blows out a frustrated breath. Her hands are shaking.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Fine. Okay. I didn't find anything else, but Koslova did. She was tagging after the Angle Grinders, and found the Director's personal log.

Chief Ibanez:

 What? Where? I'm sure I would have seen that, unless there's doors in here that only open to skinny women with fat knives.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It was in that airlock that opens on stone.

Chief Ibanez:

 I must have been in there twenty times. For…

<Chief Ibanez winces, then strikes herself in the side of the head. Both of the doctors instinctively jolt in their chairs, reaching for her before lowering their hands again and frowning.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Reasons. God damn it, it still hurts. I remember, but it 

fucking

 hurts.

<She takes a deep breath.>

Chief Ibanez:

 But I'm sure I wouldn't have missed a thing like that. I was collecting everything important.

<Dr. Astrauskas pauses.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I don't think it was in there when you were.

Chief Ibanez:

 What the hell is that supposed to mean?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Take a look.

<She removes a data pad from her jacket, and hands it to Chief Ibanez. The pad is an unfamiliar make and model, and the rubber slipcase carries the insignia of the Secure Containment Institute.>

<Chief Ibanez begins to read.>

Personal Log of J. ██████, Director, Facility-34

01/09/1994

We don't know much more about these people now than we did six months ago. They keep to themselves, which is good; we could enforce a curfew, probably, but it's better not to need to. Our resources are over-committed as it is. They answer our questions politely enough, even though half the time the answer is "no", as in "no, I'm not going to tell you about that". One thing is clear: they aren't from around here. Even though almost all of them are obviously Argentinean, and most of them speak Spanish. Their hovels are a whole lot older than makes any sense, and it's completely impossible to trace any of their bloodlines, and no progress has been made on answering the biggest, most brightly burning question: how the hell did they manage to stay hidden for so long? Whatever it was they were doing, they aren't doing it now. They rely on us to hush it all up, which I guess is the price we pay for nosing in.

The fact is, they're not nearly the strangest or most foreign thing on our soil today. It's starting to look like every corner of South America is haunted, and we're getting reports of potential anomalies in Asia, Europe, and even up north now. A few more years and we might need to think about spreading the net a lot wider. Global coordination. A thicker blanket between civilization and the spooky stuff on the outskirts.

If that happens, I wonder how long we'll be content to let these people keep their secrets.

 

 

06/04/1994

It's getting rough out there. Caught with our pants down. I'm not sure we can win this thing.

They came to me today, with a confession and a plan. The confession was a lot.

The plan is everything.

 

 

06/29/1994

They'll all be dead by now. Everybody who isn't in here with me. All gone.

I always thought it would start suddenly, and end the same. Maybe a few hours between the first whimper and the final bang. We'd just started scraping the surface of the world, just barely caught a glimpse of what lies beneath, but we saw enough to know how very outclassed we all were. Too few rowers against too strange a current. It could only ever end one way.

I knew better than to pray for painless, but quick? I thought quick would be assured.

It took decades, 

decades,

 but we're finally snowed under. We can't hold it back anymore. The entire world will freeze over, or burn, or whatever it is they're trying to accomplish. If we'd had more time, it would have been different. More people. More knowledge.

And that, of course, is why I'm here.

They'll all be dead by now. That's the precondition. If they'd finished up under Yellowstone, we might have had a second option. But they didn't, so we don't. So I put out the call, gathered everyone I could — neighbors included, since this is really their rodeo — and now I'm sitting here with one metaphorical finger on that very real, very big red button.

The doors are shut. We've got all the time we need. So I thought I should at least make a record, you know? Put down any metaphors that occurred to me, capture the mood of the moment. I can do it up decently once the dust settles, or find a better writer who can sort out a more fitting epitaph.

My words are spent. I guess it's time to go.

See you on the other side, you sons of bitches.

We'll be ready when you swing back around, mark my words.

 

 

??/??/????

They're all dead.

For real, this time. My people, the ones who were going to make it. They trusted me, and that turned out to be just another in our long line of mistakes. The exchangers didn't work. They weren't prepared for the shift. There's a corpse in every corner now, blood leaking out of their ears. I'm the only one who survived.

You wouldn't think a hundred dead would be so bad after six billion. But I knew these people, so it matters more. Isn't that disgusting?

Maybe I can find a way to breed that sort of tribalism out of us. Lord knows I've got the time, now.

Only I don't, do I? I'm young, but I'm not getting any younger. I need to get moving, but I'm afraid to open those doors. I don't even know what this part of the world is like, in this period. Are there other people around? Will I be able to explain what I need, to them? Will we even speak the same language?

I had people who knew these things. I should have talked to them more often.

What I do have is The Severed. Not a single one of them failed to make the passage. Their leader reminds me her ancestors have done it before; that's how they helped us to make the machine, after all. She tells me she can still help, they all can. She assures me there will be continuity.

I don't care about continuity.

At this price, I demand 

change

.

 

 

~1500

At some point, everyone thinks about what they'd do with a second chance. What they'd do differently. What mistakes they'd avoid. What ones they wouldn't. It's always stuff like "I'd make my mom quit smoking", or "I'd get diagnosed sooner", or "I'd handle that relationship better". But nobody ever has to put those plans into place, because there are no second chances. Nobody ever comes up against the fact that you don't just get to improve this thing, or that thing, or the other, you have to relive 

everything in between

 as well, and get it right too. That would be a hell of a program to have to code. Making it work as a fallible human being? Completely ridiculous. That's why the whole thing can never be anything but a hypothetical.

And yet, here I am. At square one. With the whole sorry mess both behind and ahead of me. The vaguest sense of what went wrong, and an even vaguer idea of how I might help set it right. Potential allies, all of them dealing with a similar sort of loss. But at least they have a road map, and maybe we have each other. I don't know.

I think I'm going to spend a week or two losing my mind, first. As a palate cleanser.

I hoped I'd remember more.

It's all just flashes and intimation. I can gather a lot from what I wrote, but I didn't write a lot.

Maybe it will be enough.

But for who?

 

 

02/13/1867

I'm dying.

But it doesn't matter. The legacy is secure.

We gave him everything, in the end. For his part, he gave us a lot. It was an equitable trade, considering the circumstances, and I trust him to make the most of it. There's a long, long road ahead, but he will know — our children will know — what's waiting for them at the end. If not the specifics, then the general gist.

And they'll know it's their job to stop it.

We can't stay in here. The cracks are showing. Not wide, yet, but wide enough some day to swallow us all up. The bay will suffice, until it's time to move again.

Maybe it won't ever be time. That would be lovely.

But I'll never know.

So I just have to hope.

If anyone's reading this:

Get

 

it

 

right

 

this

 

time

.

 

 

Personal Log of T. ██████, Director, Facility-34

04/01/1867

An era ends.

The next won't last nearly so long.

But it won't be any less busy.

 

 

Personal Log of N. ██████, Director, Facility-34

03/18/1879

We're finally able to start fixing some of the things in here. I estimate we'll have most of the equipment repaired decades before it would be possible to invent it.

 

 

Personal Log of R. ██████, Director, Facility-34

07/09/1969

The difference we've made is extraordinary. The only thing more difficult than nudging history in the right direction is occluding the origin of the push.

Humanity is standing in a crowd of faceless horrors, and we're elbowing them toward the fire exit.

 

 

Personal Log of O. ██████, Director, Facility-34

09/02/1975

This place has almost outlived its usefulness. That was always part of the plan, but it's honestly a surprise to see it happen. People have lived and died in here without ever knowing for sure that everything was going to work out.

I've had to turn on the occlusion system. It's finicky, and I don't know how long it will last, but I can't take the chance of some satellite picking us up. The limitations are frightening, but at least nobody else knows how to weaponize them. I hope.

The Facility should be self-sustaining now. We're going to leave the keys in the ignition, just in case, but I think the next time I walk out those doors will be the last time.

I hope nobody ever needs to go back in.

Because that will mean we didn't get it right this time, either.

 

 

Personal Log of L. ██████, Director, Facility-34

06/29/1994

Someone's been in here.

I can't find the Director's keycard. I think it might be gone. There's places in here we wouldn't be able to cut our way into if we spent a decade on it. We're shut out.

The machine is broken, and the flowers are wilting. We were able to get into parts storage, and Ricardo thinks he can get it working again. But it's going to be a one-way trip.

I just hope we haven't got a stowaway.

But I don't think we can afford to keep looking. The dilation isn't the same as it was before. Whatever's wrong with the machine, it's spreading. They're seeing things in the corridors. It's getting harder to talk. Time is running every which way. When I check the monitor, it seems like outside is catching up. We need to be out of here before they realize we're gone. Before they kill whoever's trying to kill them.

 

 

06/30/1994

They're all dead.

I have to believe that, because anything else would paralyze me.

I have to save what's left.

I have to press the button.

Dad. Teresa. Ernesto. Jorge. Aurelio. Eloy. Fina. Yésica.

I'm so sorry.

<Dr. Okorie, now standing, places a hand on Chief Ibanez's shoulder.>

Chief Ibanez:

 They were here.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 They were here 

after I was here.

<Dr. Astrauskas stands, and places a hand on Chief Ibanez's other shoulder.>

Chief Ibanez:

 They left me.

<Chief Ibanez shakes them both off, and marches toward the operations centre.>

Chief Ibanez:

 They're alive.

<Transcript ends.>

Addendum 8273-9, Free Port Consult:

 On 01/16/2024, prior to embarking on Operation CICLO, Chief Ibanez consulted with Queen Aphora of FP-09 on the topic of the supposed "Prophets of the Severed Halls." A partial transcript of their interview is appended below, for context.

<Excerpt begins.>

<Aphora stands at the pinnacle of the Palace of Aph. The sandstone has been scoured of all decoration, and the furnishings are spare and simple. A wraparound window covers the south wall, beyond which the remainder of the city can be seen. It is badly damaged, though massive clouds of dust mark the locations of Aphian micamancers engaged in reconstruction work. The most urgent activity is around the city walls, which suffered extensive damage during the city's extrusion from the earth.>

<Chief Ibanez approaches, and stands beside Aphora at the window.>

Aphora:

 Come to see the harm your lover wrought personally, now that the dust has settled?

Chief Ibanez:

 The dust is never settled with you.

Aphora:

 It will certainly never be settled between us.

Chief Ibanez:

 Suits me fine.

<She taps the glass.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Repairs seem to be going well.

<Aphora grunts.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Udo told me she intentionally cushioned everything in as much sand as she could before she brought it up through the crust. As far as I can see, most of the city made it out intact.

Aphora:

 Most. I'll note she made precious little effort to preserve our walls.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah, well. As I think she'd remind you, walls make bad neighbours.

Aphora:

 You came here to reinforce her ill-considered, heavy-handed lectures on responsibility?

Chief Ibanez:

 I came here to talk about the Severed Halls. You said there was more to the story.

Aphora:

 I did say that. I also said it wasn't mine to tell.

Chief Ibanez:

 You're in this conflict now, Aphora. There's no weaseling out of it. If there's another involved party, one we don't know about…

Aphora:

 You want to find them, ruin their homes too?

Chief Ibanez:

 I want to know what part they're going to play.

<Aphora sighs.>

Aphora:

 Their part concluded long ago. As I told… 

Dr. Okorie,

 they were seers.

Chief Ibanez:

 They prophesied.

Aphora:

 Yes.

Chief Ibanez:

 When did your people break with the prophets?

Aphora:

 Long, long ago. Before I was born.

Chief Ibanez:

 Which was when?

Aphora:

 About 1500.

Chief Ibanez:

 Isn't that when the Unyielding and Uncontained were created?

Aphora:

 That's one theory.

Chief Ibanez:

 You're going to try and be cagey with me? I've still got access to that orbital kill satellite.

Aphora:

 And you won't use it, so long as you think there's a chance you can wring more information out of me. Consider my recalcitrance an investment in my own future.

Chief Ibanez:

 I just consider it annoying. But fine, we'll put a pin in that. 

Why

 did you break with the prophets?

Aphora:

 They became selfish.

Chief Ibanez:

 Not like you guys.

Aphora:

 Precisely not like us. They felt guilty about those we left behind. And so we had to leave them.

Chief Ibanez:

 You dumped your conscience on the side of the multiversal road, huh?

Aphora:

 They were not our conscience. They were a floating, omnidirectional sense of guilt. It bound them together. And that was the source of their power.

Chief Ibanez:

 How so?

Aphora:

 They knew each other. They were connected by those inextricable strands of responsibility. In tandem, they could move as one. Like I said, selfish.

Chief Ibanez:

 You and I define that word differently. What kind of mobility are we talking, here?

Aphora:

 The kind for which the ends of the Earth prove no barrier.

Chief Ibanez:

 You mean…?

Aphora:

 Their rituals were vital to our escape. We had to develop a means of our own, when they were gone.

Chief Ibanez:

 You're saying they were the ones who made the city move? Who saved you from your universe exploding?

Aphora:

 Yes.

<Silence on recording.>

Aphora:

 That troubles you.

Chief Ibanez:

 No, it's just…

Aphora:

 Why? What connection have you just made?

Chief Ibanez:

 Where did you leave them?

Aphora:

 Why does it matter? They won't let you find them.

Chief Ibanez:

 It matters because… I think…

<Chief Ibanez takes a deep breath.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I think they did to me, what you did to them.

<Excerpt ends.>

Addendum 8273-10, Additional Consult:

 Immediately after updating the SCP-8273 file with Addendum 8273-8, PTF Delta-6500 received a directive from the Department of Containment barring them from further investigating the implications of the Facility-34 Director's personal log beyond the scope of the present subject. Chief Ibanez's earlier consultation request, to assess the state of the Facility's dimensional travel mechanism, was granted; the circumstances of the consultant's arrival are outlined in the transcript below.

<Transcript begins.>

<Chief Ibanez and Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie watch as an MTF Epsilon-43 helicopter lands on the Zevalan beach, and Dr. Placeholder McDoctorate emerges. He waves excitedly and attempts to speak, then begins coughing in the cloud of sand raised by the rotors. He is inaudible until the helicopter departs again.>

Dr. Placeholder McDoctorate.

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I said, the band's back together, huh?

<Dr. Okorie smiles, and waves. Dr. McDoctorate waves back.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Are you alone? I was expecting a real scientist, too.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'm a real…

<Dr. McDoctorate scowls.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'm not just a pataphysicist. I'm a hardware and software engineer, as well as a quantum theorist. I built the 

REISNO Cannon

, remember? And I've been thinking of getting back into that sort of thing lately. You know, crazy machines.

<Dr. McDoctorate chuckles.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I love crazy machines.

<He notices something over Chief Ibanez's shoulder, and suddenly grins.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Oh, hey! You brought the thing. I've been asking to study that for 

ages.

 How'd you get it out of the DoC's clutches?

Chief Ibanez:

 Sokolsky.

.

Dr. Daniil Sokolsky, Deputy Director of the Emergent Threat Tactical Response Authority.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Yeah. Figures.

<The four of them head up the path toward Facility-34.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What did you want to study it for?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Are you kidding? The pataphysics sword?

<Chief Ibanez huffs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Not this again.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It's an artifact that catalyzes your protagonistic potential into a source of renewable anomalous energy. It's quite possibly the coolest thing I've ever seen that doesn't have moving parts or code. Why did you bring it?

<They have reached the entrance to the Facility. Dr. McDoctorate's eyes widen.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Oh, wow. You brought it to make this place appear, didn't you?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I'm still not clear why it worked.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Well, it's obvious, isn't it?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 No. That's why I said I'm not clear on it.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Sorry. Sorry. I mean… are you familiar with the trope of the doomed hometown?

 Are you familiar with the trope of the expert who dies early?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'm familiar with 

all the tropes,

 but I don't think there's a name for that one. Anyway, it'd be 

sudden sequel death syndrome

 in this case. What was I saying?

 Doomed hometown.

<Dr. McDoctorate extends his arms wide for emphasis.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Right. One of the most common launching pads for a hero. Heading out into a brave new future, with the past on fire behind them. But today, she came back.

<Dr. McDoctorate claps. Dr. Astrauskas jumps.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 The arc is completed. That's powerful.

Dr. Okorie:

 That's not what it was.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 No?

Dr. Okorie:

 No.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Then what?

<Dr Okorie glances at Chief Ibanez, who is looking at the sky.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Ask me later. Can you fix the machine?

<Dr. McDoctorate shrugs.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Maybe? From the outline you sent it's not like anything I've ever seen, but then, that goes for all eigenmachines. Having the sword here will help, assuming my techno-wizardry counts as a kind of heroics.

Chief Ibanez:

 Weak assumption.

<Dr. McDoctorate heads for the Facility, ignoring her.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Anyway, leave it with me.

<He glances over his shoulder, and raises a finger.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 But keep that sword charged, just in case.

<Five hours have passed. Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie are playing double solitaire in the control room. Chief Ibanez is sitting across the room, her back to the others.>

Dr. Okorie:

 I have a semantics question.

<Dr. Astrauskas nods. Chief Ibanez does not move.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Does 'no further investigation' mean we can't chat about it?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I mean, we'd only be talking about the investigation we already did.

Dr. Okorie:

 Cool.

<She throws down her cards.>

Dr. Okorie:

 WHAT THE FUCK.

<Chief Ibanez glances over at her, but still does not respond.>

<Dr. Okorie stands, and begins pacing operations control.>

Dr. Okorie:

 We know what it means, right? What it has to mean? It can only—

Dr. Astrauskas:

 WHAT THE FUCK!

<Dr. Okorie jumps, and glares at Dr. Astrauskas.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Sorry. I've got a longer fuse. Yeah, this is too much. We have to talk about it.

Dr. Okorie:

 Okay.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Alright.

Dr. Okorie:

 So, we know the world is kind of ending. Because of the cycle.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Yeah.

Dr. Okorie:

 And we learned last year that other worlds have ended before, because of the same thing.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Right. And you and your mom are descendants of escapees from some of those other worlds.

Dr. Okorie:

 Right.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 So is it that weird to find out someone time travelled from one of those other worlds to found the Foundation?

<Silence on recording.>

Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie:

 (in unison) YES!

<Chief Ibanez sighs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Who cares?

<They glance in her direction. She does not meet their eyes.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Del…

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I'm sorry. It's just, it's a lot. I know that you…

<She raises her hands, then slaps them to her thighs in frustration.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I know.

 It's fine.

Chief Ibanez:

 It's whatever.

Dr. Okorie:

 Del—

 Fuck off.

 Multiversal travel must have weakened the glass. That stuff in the diary about exchangers—

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Did you cut yourself? Let me—

Chief Ibanez:

 FUCK OFF!

<She shoves them away from her, slams the doors fully open, and storms into the corridor.>

<There is an exclamation of surprise and pain, in a male voice, and Chief Ibanez shouts in inarticulate rage.>

<Dr. McDoctorate appears in the doorway, rubbing his hip. He looks down at the broken glass.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Bad time?

<Dr. Okorie purses her lips.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Well, uh. So.

<Chief Ibanez pushes roughly past him again, into operations control. She pulls a chair away from a monitoring console with enough force to briefly lift it from the floor, slams it down, and sits.>

<Silence on recording.>

<Chief Ibanez clenches her jaw.>

Chief Ibanez:

 WELL?

<Dr. McDoctorate blinks, then gently pulls out a second chair on the other side of the double doors, and sits down. The other two doctors lean on the backs of the nearest aisle consoles, looking back and forth between Chief Ibanez and Dr. McDoctorate.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 So, there's a problem.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Just the one?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Well, just the one we can do anything about. The Facility has a variety of defensive systems I don't fully understand, and I'm just going to say right out that there's no chance I 

will

 understand them any time soon. There's no documentation, and several of them have become disused to the point of being fancy-looking slag. Between metal fatigue and the effects of our SRAs, time dilation is now almost nil and I don't see that ever changing. And if any of these doohickeys put up that dome people saw during TAILWIND KITE, that dome is staying down. For now, at least.

<He gives her a wry, if cautious, look.>

Dr. McDoctorate

 Though I suspect you don't need or particularly want help on the defensive front.

Chief Ibanez:

 No. Focus on the things I can't do on my own.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Big ticket item it is. I've got most of the mechanism figured out.

<Dr. Okorie frowns.>

Dr. Okorie:

 How? How can you possibly?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Don't get me wrong. I don't know why this thing does what it presumably does—

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What does it presumably do?

<Chief Ibanez crosses her arms, and looks at the ceiling.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Well, it's called the Trans-Liminal Propulser — which is not what I would call very good English, by the way — so it presumably travels between universes. Whether that's alternate timelines, alternate universes, or tangents, I have no idea. Just like I have no idea how it's capable of doing that. Which, by the way, holy shit! Had to get that out of the way.

Dr. Okorie:

 How dare you.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Sorry. But anyway, what I 

do

 know is what a machine looks like when it's properly ticking over, and this one is getting there fast. It was mostly just wear and tear. Like somebody took the old jalopy for a spin one time too many.

Chief Ibanez:

 Somebody.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Yeah.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 The other thing that happens when you don't do the required maintenance on your vehicle.

Dr. Okorie:

 Your stickers expire?

 You run out of fuel.

Dr. Okorie:

 Oh. I don't do a lot of driving.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Basement dwellers.

 What's it run on?

 Visions.

<The other three turn to face her.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Eh?

 Stranger-in-the-Mist. They use it for visions.

 Flower power.

Addendum 8273-11, Transit:

 With the arrival of technical specialists from Site-34 the following day and ontokinetics personnel from Site-120 the day after, Dr. McDoctorate's assessment and repair work proceeded at a rapid pace. Chief Ibanez conducted training exercises and minor off-site operations coordinated with Latin American Branch Command, while Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie maintained operational control at Caleta San Roque. Chief Ibanez returned five days after Dr. McDoctorate's arrival to provide additional engineering consults, and two days later the final adjustments had been made.

The device's computer controls were activated in full, and after a further day familiarizing themselves with the operating system and interface and running diagnostics — with Chief Ibanez's memories of her earlier trips now fully restored — it was determined by Delta-6500 that all was in order.

Chief Ibanez assembled her command personnel in operations control to begin the exploratory component of Operation CICLO. A transcript of their brief discussion is appended below.

<Transcript begins.>

<Chief Ibanez stands in front of the central board. Drs. Astrauskas, McDoctorate and Okorie stand behind the front row of consoles.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Today's the day?

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah. Assuming poofy fixed the exchangers.

<Dr. McDoctorate reaches up to finger his curly hair, mouthing the word 'poofy' with a frown.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 They're fixed, yes. I take great pride in the fact that my projects never result in 

everyone dying.

Chief Ibanez:

 Just thought I'd ask.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Haven't seen much of you these past few.

Chief Ibanez:

 Been busy. Nobody but me has ever used the thing before.

Dr. Okorie:

 And yet you've been flying around the countryside for most of the last week. Del, are you—

Chief Ibanez:

 I want to get this over with. I don't stand around waiting for things to happen. They can happen now, so I'm here. I'm ready. Are you?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It might be prudent to give anyone who's taking the trip a psych workup. Looking for stress. Even a proper aura reading—

Chief Ibanez:

 You think there's any chance this boat leaves without me?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 No, but—

Chief Ibanez:

 You think I'm fragile? Udo, you think that?

Dr. Okorie:

 We know you aren't.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 You do seem very angry, though. That could cloud your judgement.

<Chief Ibanez nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm the ranking combatant. I'm in charge of any security aspects. You and Udo have scientific control, and I don't rank either of you. Roz has last say on psych matters. That enough ass-covering for you?

Dr. Okorie:

 Nobody's trying to cover—

Chief Ibanez:

 I hate this. I always hate this shit. You think you have to say this, but it won't change anything. I'm going. You're going. Any conversation we could have will just delay the inevitable.

Dr. Okorie:

 We've 

delayed the inevitable

 before. You and me, and Place. And the Leading Edge. You can get a lot done in an interval, sometimes.

Chief Ibanez:

 Not this time. If there's work worth doing now, it's on the other side.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 We still don't really know much about that other side. The controls make it easy enough to backtrack to the Facility's last stop, and it's one you've been to before according to your notes on the manual and the recordings you made, but…

Chief Ibanez:

 But?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 But all you did was go for a swim and eat some fish. Three decades ago. Who knows what we're going to see on the other side, really?

Chief Ibanez:

 That's why we're putting a limit on our losses. Us four, as many techs as you need, and a couple agents from 6500. Everybody else stands well back and hopes nothing explodes.

Dr. Okorie:

 Wouldn't it be safer to bring everyone?

Chief Ibanez:

 Safer for us. Not safer for everyone. A small team might be vulnerable, but if it's really bad wherever we end up, and we get overwhelmed, I want as much brain and brawnpower on this side trying to get us back as possible.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 So you're leaving the sword?

<Chief Ibanez scoffs.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Didn't think so.

Chief Ibanez:

 The supplies I wanted are stocked?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Food, meds, and about half Puerto Extraño's crop of 

Nigella.

 But I know you checked already.

Chief Ibanez:

 Never hurts to double-check. Whatever's waiting for us, I doubt there's a corner grocery.

<She thumbs her lapel radio.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You there, Nasty?

Agent Koslova:

 Setting up shop. Ready in five.

Chief Ibanez:

 Place?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Essential personnel are already inside, and everyone else is at the camp.

Chief Ibanez:

 Good boy. Go tell your folks the game is on, and then meet us at the big red button.

Dr. Okorie:

 Is it actually a big red button?

Chief Ibanez:

 You heard the recording. I really was hoping for a bomb.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It still might be one.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It won't blow up. More likely it smears our atoms across the timeplane.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It not doing that is even more likely, though, right?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'd say yes.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 That's a relief.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 In the confidence that if I'm wrong, you won't be able to complain to me about it after.

<The Trans-Liminal Propulser (TLP) is a fountain cluster of chrome pipes surrounded by a glittering net of fibre optics, both sets of tubes emerging from a central spiral shaft descending down beneath the floor to disappear into a mass of jet intakes, coolant tanks, and computer banks. The control room looks down on the machine from above.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I love this thing. So elegant.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I'm still amazed you guys got it back in order so fast.

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm not.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Well, sure, you've seen it before, but that was ages ago. And Place never saw it at all.

Dr. Okorie:

 Do we know that?

<Chief Ibanez nods fractionally.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 If this was constructed in the 1990s in a universe not too much different from this one, it's remotely conceivable I could have been involved in the project. Probably as a programmer. The code was suspiciously simple to untangle. The thought did occur to me.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Well, that's kind of creepy.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Let's agree to call it auspicious instead, eh? For luck.

Chief Ibanez:

 We good?

Dr. McDoctorate looks down at the main console.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Board is green. Red's all yours.

<He steps aside to let her take his place.>

<She keys her mic.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Hold on to your atoms.

<She releases the mic, and takes a deep breath.>

<In a single fluid motion she steps up to the console and presses the activation switch.>

<The shaft begins to turn, and the fibre optics shimmer with colour. All sound ceases. There is a bright light. It resolves into static; later examination will reveal this to be a representation of cosmic background radiation. The visible spectrum abruptly compresses on the vertical axis, then horizontally at a slower pace, as with a collapsing cathode ray tube image. There is darkness for several seconds, then the process reverses. The static returns; its profile has shifted to an unfamiliar configuration. All camera feeds now resolve to show the control room again. All parties appear unharmed.>

<Dr. Okorie speaks first, barely above a whisper.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Wheeee.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I was really hoping for a 'vwoorp', at least.

<Dr. McDoctorate gently eases Chief Ibanez aside, and examines the readout.>

<Without waiting for a verdict, Chief Ibanez leaves the room. The others follow, Dr. McDoctorate bringing up the rear.>

<Agents Koslova and Koslov join the group as they approach the rear airlock. They do not speak.>

<The others hang back as Chief Ibanez walks through the inner airlock door, opens a storage locker, and removes SCP-6500-SWORD in its sheathe. She attaches the sheathe to its harness, and shoulders it on.>

<She places a finger on the outer door release.>

<She whispers something inaudible, and cycles the airlock.>

<The inner door closes.>

<Gases exchange.>

<The outer door opens.>

<Beyond, all is green.>

<Transcript ends.>

Addendum 8273-12, Arrival:

 With confirmation from Chief Ibanez that the exterior environment was safe in an immediate sense, instruments were set up by the skeleton scientific staff to determine atmospheric conditions in greater detail. It was quickly determined that the Facility's destination, topographically similar to the gulch on Caleta San Roque but densely overgrown with unfamiliar vegetation, had the same atmospheric content as the planet Earth — minus environmental pollutants, which were negligible.

PTF Delta-6500, now consisting of Chief Ibanez, Drs. Astrauskas, McDoctorate and Okorie, and agents Koslov and Koslova, therefore began exploration of the new environment.

<Transcript begins.>

<Delta-6500 are moving through the gulch. The vegetation is thick, but they are able to make slow progress toward the beach. The exterior of the Facility behind them is still pristine, but there is a pile of rotting plant material at the base of its walls, suggesting overgrowth which fell and decayed when SCP-6500-SWORD called the Facility back to baseline reality. There is a rut in the ground, suggesting frequent traffic between beach and Facility at some point in the past, but this too is thickly overgrown. The sky is a yellowish green. There are no clouds.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Do you remember anything yet?

<Chief Ibanez shrugs noncommittally. Her shoulders are tense.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 She's been out two hours, and she never did much here the first time around. She probably remembers everything.

<Agent Koslova draws a sharp breath. The doctors stop moving; Chief Ibanez and Agent Koslov do not.>

Dr. Okorie:

 You hear something?

Agent Koslova:

 Sorry, just inhaling. Air's so god damn clean.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Spores, though.

<She points up. Above the gulch, the sky is now mottled with thick blobs floating on a light breeze, darker green than the sky.>

<Agent Koslov points his flashlight up at the spores, and activates it. The spores shine brightly in the light. When he turns it off, the glow remains for some time.>

<Agent Koslova smacks him in the back of the head.>

Agent Koslova:

 Idiot. They'll know we're coming now.

Chief Ibanez:

 They already know.

<At the far end of the gulch, a young woman is standing stock still. She is dressed in typical 1990s casual clothing, careworn and repaired in places. She is staring at the party, open-mouthed.>

SCP-8273-2:

 Oh my god?

<Both agents have their hands on their holstered weapons. Chief Ibanez presses her hands to her thighs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Identify yourself.

SCP-8273-2:

 Oh my 

god.

Chief Ibanez:

 Not me, you.

SCP-8273-2:

 What…?

Chief Ibanez:

 Tell me who you are, kid.

<Chief Ibanez approaches the woman. Her eyes are a dark green, matching the verdant gulley in the fading light.>

SCP-8273-2:

 Pilar. I… my name is Pilar. Oh my god, where did you come from? Did my dad…?

SCP-8273-2.

Chief Ibanez:

 We're with the SCP Foundation. I'm Chief Delfina Ibanez.

<Pilar blinks.>

Pilar:

 Delfina?

Chief Ibanez:

 Ibanez.

Pilar:

 Ibanez. Oh my god.

Chief Ibanez:

 You've said that. A few times.

Dr. Okorie:

 This is going to be a lot for them to process, Del.

Chief Ibanez:

Pilar:

 Others? What…?

<Chief Ibanez snaps her fingers rapidly.>

Chief Ibanez:

 The dizzy bitch routine is really starting to get on my nerves. Are you alone, or are there others?

Pilar:

 There's others.

<Pilar looks back to where the gulch should turn to meet the beach.>

Pilar:

 At the village.

Chief Ibanez:

 The village.

Pilar:

 That's right. Past the cleft, and up the beach.

Chief Ibanez:

 The cleft, and the beach.

Pilar:

 That's right. I, I can take you there. Oh my god, you're really…? And you're from… Earth?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Meaning that's not where this is.

<Pilar shakes her head emphatically.>

Pilar:

 No. Not at all.

Chief Ibanez:

 What's this place called, then?

Pilar:

 Puerto Extirpado.

<Chief Ibanez sucks in a breath through her teeth.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Del?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 What's it mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 It's not exact.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Contextually, then.

<Chief Ibanez grits her teeth.>

Chief Ibanez:

 The Severed Port.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Guess that answers that.

<Chief Ibanez gestures at Pilar.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Well, don't just stand there gaping. Lead on.

<Pilar steps back, and waits for Chief Ibanez to approach her. The others follow at a distance. Pilar leads the group farther down the gulch, to where it should narrow to a cleft if the stone facing mirrors that of Caleta San Roque.>

Pilar:

 I can't believe you're here.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

Pilar:

 I know who you are.

Chief Ibanez:

 Uh huh.

Pilar:

 You're supposed to be dead.

Chief Ibanez:

 Everyone from Zevala is supposed to be dead.

<Pilar frowns.>

Pilar:

 How did you get here?

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm only gonna explain this once. Not ten thousand times.

Pilar:

 There's only seventy-two of us.

Chief Ibanez:

 Seventy-two.

Pilar:

 Yeah.

<Chief Ibanez removes her service weapon from its holster. Pilar's eyes widen, and she raises her hands as if in self-defence. Chief Ibanez begins a systematic weapon check as they proceed toward the cleft.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Del—

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Don't.

Dr. Okorie:

 I just—

Dr. Astrauskas:

 No.

<Dr. Astrauskas points at herself.

>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Trust me. Don't.

<Chief Ibanez finishes checking her weapon as the party reaches the cleft, and secures it in its holster again. Pilar looks at her warily as she leads the party onto the beach, single file with Chief Ibanez immediately behind her.>

<The sand appears greyish, but this is likely a property of the greenish light. There is no visible sun when the bay comes into view, as the sky is hazy, but judging by the darkening landscape it appears to be setting behind the distant cliffs. These cliffs are much higher than the matching cliffs of Caleta San Roque, an average of perhaps fifty metres from the bay to the table, and two hundred from the table to the tops of the hills, but they obey the same general shape. There is vegetation consistent with thick tree cover, though it is impossible to determine species at this distance. The waters of the bay are completely still, and algae green.>

<Across the bay and to the right where the table encircles it, lights are visible. The rough shape of irregular shacks can be discerned, as well as grain silos, a tall windmill, a badly canted lighthouse and the barely-visible wreck of a rusted cargo ship.>

<Chief Ibanez walks to the edge of the water, and stares at the lights.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Del? Is this it?

<There is no response.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Del?

Puerto Extirpado.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

<Chief Ibanez turns, not to face them, but to approach the path up the table at the northern end of the beach.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah, this is it.

<It is night in Puerto Extirpado as Delta-6500 and Pilar leave the beach and head up the table's eastern incline. Construction is sparse here; the group pass through the remains of a gatehouse composed of sheets of corrugated metal in various colours, largely overgrown with broad-leaved ivies of no Earthly clade. There are a few huts of similar construction here, though most are equally overgrown and several show signs of severe fire damage.>

<There are lanterns hanging from the less disused structures, burning a sickly yellow. The lights multiply farther up the incline, and the structures are in better repair. Here they have been augmented with hewn and painted wood, possibly replacing damage to the original steel.>

<There is a brighter light ahead, and a thin older woman carrying a lantern appears on the well-beaten path. Pilar rushes ahead of the party to meet her.>

SCP-8273-4:

 Pilar! It's late! Where have you…

SCP-8273-4:

 …

dios mio.

 Mother!

SCP-8273-4:

 Nobody's in charge.

<The older woman, apparently Ursula, simply stares at her.>

<Chief Ibanez walks past her to a large brass bell mounted on a wooden swinging mount. She turns a crank, and the bell begins to swing. It peals out across the bay.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Alarm bells. Could have used these before.

Ursula:

 That's why we have them now. Are you…

<There are suddenly tears in her eyes.>

Ursula:

 It can't be.

<Chief Ibanez walks past her without a word.>

<Dr. Okorie approaches the older woman.>

Dr. Okorie:

 It's a weird day for her.

Pilar:

 Weirder for us.

<Chief Ibanez passes Ursula, and begins to climb the eastern slope.>

SCP-8273-4.

<Delta-6500 and the two Extirpadan women move through the eastern end of the village towards the town hall at the rough centre of its arc. The east is poorly-populated, with most well-lit houses clustered around the centre and the west. Residents in worn clothing emerge from the shacks as the party passes by, and Ursula and Pilar direct some of them to the town hall. Most already seem to know where they should go, though all regard the new arrivals with a mixture of curiosity and shock as they do. A word from Ursula silences all questions.>

<The village is dotted with ruins: overgrown concrete gun emplacements, all of them badly damaged; collapsed shacks, though only the most rusted or split steel has been left behind; rotted outhouses; patches of ground where the vegetation is more or less lush, likely representing filled-in shellholes or buried items. Rusted machinery is everywhere, some of it no longer identifiable. There are also pallets of supplies, some of them weather-wrapped. There are crates similar to Foundation-issue, bearing the insignia of the Secure Containment Institute.>

<As Chief Ibanez had earlier stated, the footprints of each structure obey no rectilinear plan. All are subtly or wildly off-angle.>

<This is clearly the village of Zevala, transplanted wholesale from Caleta San Roque to Puerto Extirpado.>

<When she reaches the town hall, a much larger but no less ramshackle structure, Chief Ibanez pushes open the front double doors and enters without asking permission. Without speaking a word to Ursula or Pilar, she heads through the tidy space with its packed earthen floor and rows of gaudily-repainted 1960s-era metal chairs to hop up onto the main stage, then enter the back rooms via a heavy panelled steel door. She shuts it behind her.>

<Dr. Okorie ensures that Ursula will handle the assembling of the villagers while Agents Koslova and Koslov secure the perimeter, asserting casual authority without assuming a threatening posture. Dr. Astrauskas examines the townsfolk as they enter, smiling politely and offering little information in response to their enquiries. Dr. McDoctorate sits in a back corner, sketching and writing in a notebook and muttering quietly to himself.>

<When seventy-one villagers are assembled in the hall, including Ursula and Pilar — filling less than a quarter of the main room — Dr. Okorie climbs onto the stage and enters the back rooms without knocking.>

<Chief Ibanez is sitting at a rough-hewn table, picking at graffiti with her pen knife. The graffiti appears fresh, and takes the form of a blossoming flower, but the proportions and cuts suggest it was previously an older carving of a set of spirals in circular form.>

Chief Ibanez:

 They ready?

<She does not look up from her carving.>

Dr. Okorie:

 The old woman—

Chief Ibanez:

 Ursula.

Dr. Okorie:

 Sure, she says everyone's here who's likely to come.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why would any of them not come?

Dr. Okorie:

 I don't know.

Chief Ibanez:

 And you didn't want to ask.

Dr. Okorie:

 I'm sorry. I'm not sure what to—

<Chief Ibanez stands, closing her knife and returning it to its pouch at her belt.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It's fine. Let's go.

<The door opens again, and Dr. Astrauskas slips through.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You probably don't want to hear this—

Chief Ibanez:

 You're right.

<She walks past both doctors. After a moment, and an exchanged glance, they follow. The assembled Extirpadans look up, gasping and chattering amongst themselves. Several are pointing. Several are openly weeping.>

<Dr. Okorie closes the door behind her, and leans on it. Chief Ibanez walks up to a makeshift steel podium on casters, taller than she is, and pushes it roughly aside. It rolls to a stop just before the edge of the stage.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Alright, listen up. You…

<She blinks in the lamplight.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You…

<A voice calls out from the crowd, male.>

SCP-8273-5:

 Fina?

SCP-8273-6:

 What?

 That's Fina. That's L—

SCP-8273-7:

 That's impossible.

SCP-8273-6:

 It 

is

 Fina.

<A fourth.>

SCP-8273-8:

 Oh my god.

<Many of the villagers rise from their seats, and approach the stage. The crowd is already in an uproar.>

<Chief Ibanez stands her ground, but her posture is tense.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Back up. I don't…

<The villagers stare up at her, some grasping at the edge of the stage to get a better look. A child cries out at the back of the room, very young, and Chief Ibanez's head snaps up in shock. She moves her mouth, but no words come out.>

SCP-8273-11:

them.

<Silence on recording.>

Ursula:

 Tell us what happened.

<Chief Ibanez draws a deep breath, and fixes her eyes on a space in the far distance.>

Chief Ibanez:

SCP-8273-11:

 But is it 

you.

<She turns to face the podium, examining it, as the villagers shout questions at her and accusations at each other. She examines the scuffed black boxes at each corner of the hall, then removes her radio microphone from its lapel, winds up, and throws. The device's cord coils around the platform microphone on the podium, and she yanks, hard. The microphone falls off the podium, clattering onto the stage. An ear-splitting shriek is emitted from the speakers, and a series of loud bangs.>

As she disappears into the back rooms, Chief Ibanez again removes her radio mic from her lapel, and raises it to her mouth. She hasn't said anything before she's through the door; she closes it behind her with her free hand.>

<Transcript ends.>

Addendum 8273-13, Exploration (Puerto Extirpado):

 As night fell on Puerto Extirpado, PTF Delta-6500 were offered lodging in the town hall. Dr. Okorie accepted on behalf of Chief Ibanez, who had already exited the structure through a back door. As Agents Koslova and Koslov secured the group's gear in the back rooms, under the direction of Dr. McDoctorate, Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie searched for Chief Ibanez. They found her at the edge of the village pier.

<Transcript begins.>

<The pier now extends only a few dozen metres into the bay. The pilings had been set deep, and the surviving ones now visibly stretch down for almost sixty metres. The remains of the next few pilings can be seen below, snapped off. The water is murky, so no further remains can be seen.>

<The wreck of the

 Northern Reach 

is clearly visible to the right, stern protruding from the bay. The masts and rigging are gone, and the exposed surface is rapidly oxidizing. Algiform flora covers much of the remaining superstructure.>

<Chief Ibanez is sitting on the ragged end of the pier, which has been worn down by weather and age to a softer edge. She is looking down at the water.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I used to swim.

<Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie sit down on either side of her.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Used to?

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

<Chief Ibanez picks a small wedge of rust off the underside of the pier platform, and discs it down into the bay. There is resistance when it strikes the surface, but it eventually slides under and disappears.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Used to.

Dr. Okorie:

 I've seen you swim.

<Chief Ibanez shakes her head.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Nope.

Dr. Okorie:

 Really?

Chief Ibanez:

 Been in the water a few times on a mission, usually when it's going wrong. Had to scuba dive to nab a prisoner once. But that's it.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Why?

<Chief Ibanez looks up at the dark horizon.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Coral at the bottom of the bay used to glow. Not all one color. Whole spectrum. Sometimes like strobes on a dance floor. Sometimes it took all day to cycle; I'd poke my head down after breakfast, after lunch, after dinner, just to see the change.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You went swimming after you ate? Isn't that how you drown?

<Chief Ibanez gives her a wry look.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You drown by trying to breathe water. I was great at holding my breath. I spent hours at the bottom of that bay.

<She snorts at Dr. Astrauskas' expression.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Not all at once.

Dr. Okorie:

 I'd almost have believed you.

Chief Ibanez:

 The water was always warm. Always clean. You didn't have to go down to feel it. It blew in off the sea. Great big sheets, even when the sky was clear. I used to stand on the pier and let it wash over me. Sometimes it came in with the sunset. Jesus Christ, the sunset.

<She opens her mouth as if to laugh, but the sound doesn't come.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Yeah?

Chief Ibanez:

 Something about whatever filter was around the village. Whatever was hiding it. The sunsets were brilliant.

<She leans back on the palms of her hands.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Looked like everything was burning a little bit, from inside. Bloom from one edge of the bay to the other. And then the wind whipped the water in, and the light caught the droplets…

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Like a baptism.

Chief Ibanez:

 That's a cliché. And I didn't know what baptisms were. But I guess the idea was the same. The day washing itself away.

<She frowns.>

Chief Ibanez:

 First time I had a shower at Site-34, I broke out in hives.

Dr. Okorie:

 When was the last time you swam?

<Chief Ibanez leans forward again. She drapes her arms over her thighs, and begins undoing her bootlaces.>

Chief Ibanez:

 When Yésica and I watched the village die.

<She pauses, then begins restringing the laces, tighter.>

Chief Ibanez:

 She loved to swim. More than I did, even. Smugglers used to drop stuff overboard, for her to find. She'd dive down to the bottom and get it, and they'd let her keep what she found.

<She closes her eyes, but continues replacing the laces from memory.>

Chief Ibanez:

 She practically lived in the bay.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 And that's where she died. Bled out into the water, face down.

<Dr. Astrauskas looks down at the water. Dr. Okorie is watching Chief Ibanez very closely.>

Chief Ibanez:

 The coral doesn't glow anymore. And the sun sets the same as it does everywhere else.

<She finishes with her bootlaces, but her eyes remain closed.>

Chief Ibanez:

 The last time I touched that water, I was falling out of a helicopter. Elizabeth Crocker pushed me out. I lost consciousness, and I washed up on the shore. That's where they found me.

Dr. Okorie:

 The Foundation.

Chief Ibanez:

 I was in that water when what was left of my world disappeared. Unconscious. And it spat me back out.

<She pulls back from the edge, and climbs to her feet.>

Chief Ibanez:

 So no. I don't swim.

<Transcript ends.>
