Despite many attempts by the villagers to gain audience with Chief Ibanez, Delta-6500 spent the night in the town hall alone. Eventually the Extirpadans began returning to their homes, though curious onlookers continued to filter back in over the hours both before and after dawn.

At first light, Chief Ibanez gave instructions to her agents to assist the scientists if necessary, and struck off into the village on her own. She refused all conversation with the villagers.

Drs. Astrauskas, McDoctorate and Okorie began taking a census of Puerto Extirpado, with Ursula's help, and scheduled a series of interviews to determine the state of affairs in this alternate dimension. A digest of the results is appended below.

<Excerpt begins.>

<The sun is never visible in Puerto Extirpado except as a faint circular lightening in the sky's undifferentiated off-green haze.>

<Gualberto Parra, village elder and farm overseer, is giving Dr. Okorie a tour of the plots in the southwestern end of the village — the same location Chief Ibanez indicated on Caleta San Roque. The schoolhouse is visible farther to the west; there are two teenagers sitting in the long green grass, watched over by an older woman.>

<The farms grow squat green crops resembling squash and cabbage. Two young women in denim overalls faded almost white, with copious patching, are idly hoeing the rows and chatting in low tones.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Life on Mars.

Parra:

 Not quite so bad as you'd imagine.

Dr. Okorie:

 I wouldn't have imagined anything could grow. This place has a completely alien phylogeny. And if you could grow things, they shouldn't be edible.

Parra:

 Lucky for us we live unlikely lives, then.

Dr. Okorie:

 Very lucky. Where do you get the bulk of your supplies? Everyone I've seen seems pretty healthy.

Parra:

 Used to be, we got them out of the facility.

Dr. Okorie:

 How long did that last?

Parra:

 About a decade. There aren't very many of us, and I guess there used to be a lot of them.

<He gives Dr. Okorie a meaningful look.>

Dr. Okorie:

 I've been told in no uncertain terms not to talk about the nature of the facility.

Parra:

 So, this is going to be a one-sided conversation then.

<Dr. Okorie smiles apologetically.>

Parra:

 I can't really complain, assuming you're here to rescue us.

Dr. Okorie:

 I 

can

 tell you that's the likely plan. Do you believe me?

<Parra shrugs.>

Parra:

 I'm still waiting for you to give me a reason not to.

Dr. Okorie:

 Very fair. So, supplies from the facility. Canned goods and such?

Parra:

 And the hydroponics. All the Stranger was dead, but there was still soil and fertilizer and seeds.

Dr. Okorie:

 I didn't see any seeds.

Parra:

 That's because we used them all out here.

Dr. Okorie:

 Right. I wonder why they would have had seeds in there in the first place, though. I mean… how many kinds?

Parra:

 Hundreds.

<Dr. Okorie sighs.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Okay, there's some things I 

can

 tell you. Most of our facilities, at the Foundation, if they're big enough they have some measure of self-sufficiency. Hydroponics are pretty common. But Facility-34 doesn't look like that kind of place. There's a lot about it we don't understand, but why would they have a seed vault in there?

<She slaps her head.>

Dr. Okorie:

 I know why. And I can't tell you. I want to tell you. I'll ask, okay? If you want to know.

<Parra laughs. Dr. Okorie smiles sheepishly.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What?

Parra:

 I want to know everything, but I'm a patient guy. You'll find we're all pretty patient, I think. We've been waiting for a long, long time.

Dr. Okorie:

 I can only imagine.

<They walk to where the path splits three ways, and take the centre path. Two narrow strips of farmland pass to either side of them, the cliffs rising and falling to either side. Sounds of distant conversation carry from the school, and music can be heard across the bay.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Obviously you found the hydroponics insufficient, in the end.

Parra:

 There was a lot of very advanced technology in there, but not advanced enough to make fruits and root veg happy about growing under false light. I know people who hate tomatoes, and I know people who hate potatoes, but I don't know anybody who would be happy to go the rest of their life without both.

Dr. Okorie:

 Plus the nutritional factor.

Parra:

 Obviously that's the biggest problem. The fish helped, but there were never very many of them, and I'm sorry to say in the leaner years that we fished them right to what seems to have been their extinction. We shall not see through their like again.

<He crosses himself.>

Parra:

 We had no choice but to try transplanting the soil out here, and see what our green sun would grow. And we had some of the dirt from Zevala as well.

Dr. Okorie:

 Which I find very interesting.

<Parra shrugs.>

Parra:

 Not my area. Anyway, it took a lot of trial and error to identify anything that didn't turn brown and wilt right away. The soil here isn't bad — could be richer, could be poorer — but there's something in it that didn't like our plants very much at first. The air likes them better. The spores are like a kind of fertilizer, don't ask me how that works. We scratched out a living eventually, as you can tell from all this—

<Parra gestures at the farms.>

Parra:

 —and the fact that we haven't all starved yet.

Dr. Okorie:

 Hmm.

Parra:

 What?

Dr. Okorie:

 Let me just…

<They reach the opposite crossroads, and Dr. Okorie opens her reagents pouch.>

Dr. Okorie:

 …take a look, here.

<She sprinkles

 vim harenae 

on the soil at the far end of one of the farm plots, fans out the fingers of her right hand, and points at the little red pile. The grains vibrate, and burrow down into the earth.>

<Parra takes a step back in alarm.>

Parra:

 What are you doing?

<Dr. Okorie closes her eyes and makes slight side to side motions with her hands, as though sifting through sand. After a moment, she smiles.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Wow. Did you know there's peat deposits under your farm?

Parra:

 There's plenty of peat in the bog. What are you 

doing?

Dr. Okorie:

 It's much more fertile down there. Very fertile. I wonder if maybe there's something in the air that leaches all the nutrients out of the soil? Maybe the air is chlorophyll. Maybe the air is a living thing.

<She opens her eyes, and rotates her wrist so that her palm now faces upward. The

 vim harenae 

rises to the top of the soil again.>

Parra:

 What were you doing? With your hands?

Dr. Okorie:

 This.

<Dr. Okorie points at the

 vim harenae, 

and guides it through the air back into her reagents pouch. She laces it up as Parra stares at her in shock.>

Parra:

 What in the world.

Dr. Okorie:

 Yeah. Bet you wish you had this when you were farming.

<There is a faint rumbling beneath the earth. The farmers take wider stances, and look warily at Dr. Okorie.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What was that?

<Parra looks troubled. He stands more gingerly, as though worried the earth might shake again.>

Parra:

 It happens. Time to time. Sometimes even the mountains move.

Dr. Okorie:

 Move how?

Parra:

 Shift back and forth. We can hear the rocks falling down. There's definitely something going on down there, underground, and not everyone is convinced that it's tectonic.

Dr. Okorie:

 Something alive, you mean.

Parra:

 Could be.

Dr. Okorie:

 What about smaller predators? Birds, things like that.

Parra:

 Birds?

<He snorts.>

Parra:

 But let me answer what you're really asking: so far as we've been able to tell, there is nothing left on this Earth, if an Earth it really is, which covers itself in edible meat.

<He winces.>

Parra:

 Well, of course. Almost nothing.

<Excerpt ends.>

<Excerpt begins.>

<Dr. Astrauskas is sitting at the kitchen table in the Pelaez household. The kitchen is cluttered with bric-a-brac, but scrubbed clean; there is green residue on the outsides of the windows, but none visible indoors. Pilar Pelaez is washing breakfast dishes.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 So, this is where you were born?

Pilar:

 Yep.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What did they tell you about how the village ended up here?

<Pilar shrugs.>

Pilar:

 A lot, I think.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 But not everything?

<Pilar smiles.>

Pilar:

 Not everything. 

That,

 I know.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Anything about the facility? How it works, where it came from?

Pilar:

 Just vague stuff. Enough to understand what it is, not enough to tell you anything interesting.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 How about before? Did they tell you anything about the history of the village, back in baseline?

Pilar:

 Baseline?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Earth, you called it.

<Pilar shrugs again.>

Pilar:

 Lots about some stuff, nothing about some other stuff. You can whistle through the holes when they talk. What are you interested in?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I'm interested to know how Zevala stayed hidden for so long.

Pilar:

 Same way we stay hidden now. You must have noticed how calm it is here.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 So there's some kind of… field, maybe, hiding the village from the outside? Like back in baseline?

Pilar:

 No. It's not the village. It's us.

<She drapes her washcloth over the neck of the sink, and turns to lean against the counter.>

Pilar:

 You heard what this place is called.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Puerto Extirpado. The Severed Port.

Pilar:

 You think that means the port was severed.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It doesn't?

<Pilar shakes her head.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 By elimination I would guess that means it's the port of The Severed.

<Pilar nods.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Meaning all of you. Descendants of the Prophets of the Severed Halls of Aph.

<Pilar frowns.>

Pilar:

 Never heard anything about that. Maybe you can tell me later.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Maybe Chief Ibanez will.

Pilar:

 I didn't get the feeling she likes me very much.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 She has good reasons to be distant right now. I think you have a lot in common, though. You'll see.

<Pilar shrugs a third time, then turns back to resume the dishes.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 So, you were implying a connection between your people being The Severed and the environment not encroaching on you. And Zevala being protected.

Pilar:

 Yeah.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What are your people severed from, Pilar?

<Pilar hangs up the washcloth again, and takes a towel off a rack on the lower cabinet.>

Pilar:

 Everybody.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 In what way?

Pilar:

 In every way.

<She puts her hands on the edge of the sink, and stares at the water.>

Pilar:

 I've only heard the story once. They don't like to talk about it. But we were severed for our safety.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Cut off from the collective, then? From the human race?

<Pilar shrugs.>

Pilar:

 I guess so. I know they were able to reverse it, some sort of ritual. They did it once.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Why?

Pilar:

 You'll have to ask my mother.

<She drums her fingers on the inside of the sink basin, then suddenly stops.>

Pilar:

 Why are you staring at me like that?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You can tell?

Pilar:

 We're real good at telling when something is watching us. It's an outsider thing. Well?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I'm reading your aura.

<Pilar turns again.>

Pilar:

 What does that mean?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I'm a thaumaturge. I have magic powers.

<Pilar laughs. Dr. Astrauskas laughs with her.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I can see what mood you're in, how healthy you are. Where you're from, if I have a point of comparison. And a few other things, sometimes.

Pilar:

 What sort of other things? I'm only humouring you, by the way.

<Dr. Astrauskas gestures, wiggling her fingers.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 The breaks in your Hume spirals. The little tendrils going out of you, in every direction. You all have them. Stopping just short of each other. Reaching, but never touching.

<Pilar's brow furrows, and she reaches up to clutch her arms to her chest. She is still holding the towel.>

Pilar:

 That's not very funny.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 No. But it's very interesting.

<Excerpt ends.>

<Excerpt begins.>

<Dr. McDoctorate and Ursula are standing on a narrow metal platform at the top of the windmill tower, beside the largest grain silo. He is scanning the horizon; the tall and thickly-leaved trees of the bay stretch on over the cliffs and into the far distance, where a strange haze occludes the neighbouring territories.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 This is all very interesting.

Ursula:

 We've lived interesting lives.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Have you? I don't see any evidence of that.

<Ursula frowns.>

Ursula:

 Then what did you mean?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It's a very unusual biome. The spores grow thick and luminous at night. The sun illuminates everything, but it's behind a green screen. Things grow and the air is warm, gravity's the same as on Earth, and the cliffs are like a pre-erosion version of where Zevala was situated back home. It's interesting that this place exists, it's interesting we were able to access it, it's interesting that you've all survived, and I hear there's even more interesting things nearby that nobody bothers with. But as far as I can tell, the landscape isn't very different from the way it was back in baseline. Only… well, emptier.

<Ursula nods, and wrings the handrail.>

Ursula:

 You're not wrong. We've mostly been hanging on. It was a blow when the Facility would only make one trip. It was worse when it disappeared entirely.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 At least that was only a problem for maybe a week.

Ursula:

 More like a month.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 What?

Ursula:

 It was gone for about a month. Maybe our days are different from yours.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I don't think so. The circadian cycle seems pretty much the same. That's very odd. Is it possible the Facility needs to anchor itself, and drifts away?

Ursula:

 You tell me. You're the scientist.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Well, I only wondered if your people had more experience with it. There's some very interesting records in there. It seems like you've been connected to the Facility for a very long time.

<She nods.>

Ursula:

 My husband showed me the logs. He was the last Director, though of course that was just a ceremonial title by the end. Handed down through the family.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 You weren't in communication with the Foundation.

Ursula:

 No. We knew about it. We knew what the old logs told us about where it came from, what our part was in making it happen. But it wasn't our problem, in the end.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Why do you say that? How could a cycle of worlds ending not be everyone's problem?

Ursula:

 Zevala was a retreat. I mean that in every sense of the word. Our people were tired. Tired of struggling.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 You mean the Prophets.

<Ursula gives him an appraising look.>

Ursula:

 I'm surprised you know about them. You must have spoken to the others.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Not personally, but yes. We're in communication with Aph.

Ursula:

 Lucky you.

<In the far distance, the trees sway. There is no wind.>

Ursula:

 My ancestors didn't found Zevala as an act of surrender. They believed they could do something about what was going to happen. They tried very hard. It didn't work.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 So eventually you stopped trying.

Ursula:

 Yes. We hunkered down, and imagined ourselves safe.

<She laughs harshly.>

Ursula:

 Like a cat with its head in a paper bag. Oh.

<She smiles.>

Ursula:

 I miss cats.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I have to say, hunkering down doesn't sound like the sort of thing that would keep your village hidden as well as it was, for as long as it was.

Ursula:

 You're right. It was magic.

<She makes eye contact. He stares back at her.>

Ursula:

 I thought that might faze you.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I've been to the most magical places in the multiverse. At a run.

Ursula:

 Well. This won't sound like much to you, then. But suffice to say we have a means of making ourselves scarce, so scarce that if we were standing in the middle of that Facility, and you threw the switch, it would still leave us behind. Something in our blood that lets us reach out, or reach inside instead.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Do you still know how to do it?

Ursula:

 Of course. It's the only way we were able to come here in the first place.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 At which point I assume you… severed, yourselves again?

<She nods.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I know the TLP targets people—

Ursula:

 The what?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 The Trans-Liminal Propulser. The machine that makes everything move.

Ursula:

 Okay.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I know it targets people, but how did you get your entire village over here? All the structures and such. Even the ruins.

Ursula:

 That's my husband's area, I'm afraid. I do know it has something to do with the grainy soil beneath our buildings. We never broke ground without spreading a layer of the stuff as a foundation.

<She winces.>

Ursula:

 I wish there was another word for that.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 You think that's bad? Try to think of a second word meaning 'thing that stands in for another thing'.

<Ursula blinks, then laughs.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 The soil can't be all of it, though. I can see how some of the systems I didn't understand might target that…

<He snaps his fingers.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Aphian. That soil was mixed with Aphian sand. Udo detected it when we were examining the bay. That makes sense. Your ancestors probably brought it over from Aph itself, when they were exiled. It'll have some sort of trans-dimensional residue the TLP can pick up on. Hume declension, most likely.

<Ursula shrugs.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 But yeah, the Insurgency gun emplacements? The 

Northern Reach?

 How does the TLP target those, and bring them over?

Ursula:

 Something to do with making things uneven, but not 

too

 uneven. You must have seen the crazy angles we build our walls at. The town architect used to have a little manual she used to determine everything.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'd like to speak with her.

Ursula:

 Can any of your magicians do a séance?

<He frowns.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 None of the ones we brought with us. Anyway, I guess that mostly explains it. The Insurgency's additions were hastily-constructed, and they're loopy buggers at the best of times. Caught in your net. I understand the admonition against making things too uneven, though, because otherwise you'd end up sucking up the trees and grass and probably even the water. Sifting the village from the nature. I might have designed something similar.

Ursula:

 Ah, now I understand the company you keep.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Hmm?

Ursula:

 You're a mad scientist.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'm a mad 

polymath.

 My interests are wide-ranging. In fact, right now there's something else in particular I'm very interested in. It might sound strange.

Ursula:

 That's what strangers are for. We forgot that, to our misfortune.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 If one were to perform a mighty act in this place, something incredible, praiseworthy, something that would really change the world to a measurable extent, what would that be?

<She turns to stare at him.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I don't need an answer right away. Not until I've finished some tests. But keep it in mind, okay?

Ursula:

 Okay.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Ah…

Ursula:

 Yes?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It just occurred to me to ask. If the only living creatures the TLP targets are humans — that's correct, right?

Ursula:

 Yes.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 —and it otherwise targets irregular shapes which aren't alive…

Ursula:

 Yes?

<She waits for a moment, then suddenly realizes what he is getting at.>

Ursula:

 Oh. Well, yes. They came too.

<She points at the far side of the bay.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 And the Insurgents?

<Wordlessly, she points down at the farms.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Ah. Aha. Very… pragmatic.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 What did you mean when you said that Chief Ibanez's father was gone?

Ursula:

 Just that.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Gone dead?

Ursula:

 I wasn't sure.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 But you are now.

Ursula:

 Yes.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Why?

Ursula:

 Because Fina didn't know what I meant.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I don't understand.

Ursula:

 I thought she might have seen him.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 How?

<He makes a small exclamation of understanding.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 The Facility? You thought maybe he was the one who took it, when it disappeared.

<Ursula nods.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 So you're saying he's disappeared too, then. He might still be alive somewhere.

Ursula:

 No.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Why not?

<Ursula looks down, to where Chief Ibanez and a smaller figure are heading up the table to the west.>

Ursula:

 Because if he was, that somewhere would be here.

<Excerpt ends.>

The following is a transcript of Chief Ibanez's investigation of her family home and other locations in Puerto Extirpado during the period covered above.

<Transcript begins.>

<Chief Ibanez is walking through the Ibanez shack. Its interior is well-preserved, though the furniture and personal effects have been removed. The shack is extremely uneven in construction, all angles acute or obtuse, and the floor is hard-packed earth. As in the other shacks in Puerto Extirpado, the earth appears to originate from baseline; soil from this dimension, as with the flora, carries a distinct greenish hue absent here.>

<Chief Ibanez explores each of the three rooms, which are only differentiated by the corrugated steel walls separating them. She appears to be searching for something, but does not appear to find it.>

SCP-8273-3:

 What are you doing in here?

<Chief Ibanez does not look back at the voice, which is that of a female child, but looks out through the nearest window at the trees and the gulch beyond — a match for the one leading to her grandfather's shack in baseline.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Nothing. Why are you sneaking back there?

SCP-8273-3:

 I wasn't sneaking. But I snuck up on you.

Chief Ibanez:

 I knew you were there.

SCP-8273-3:

 Why didn't you say anything?

<Chief Ibanez turns to see a scrawny girl of perhaps ten years of age, wearing shredded blue jeans, leather boots, and a worn adult-size hooded sweater which functions as a dress given her height.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Maybe I wanted to see what you'd do if you got the drop on me.

<SCP-8273-3 laughs.>

SCP-8273-3:

 You've got a sword. I've just got sticks.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah? What do you need sticks for?

SCP-8273-3:

 To fight the dragons.

Chief Ibanez:

 Now you have my attention.

<She leans on the doorframe. SCP-8273-3 is standing in the middle of the largest room in the shack.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What's your name, kid?

SCP-8273-3:

 Saray.

Chief Ibanez:

 Pelaez, I'm guessing.

Saray:

 How'd you know?

Chief Ibanez:

 Got your mom's cheeks.

Saray:

 What's your name?

Chief Ibanez:

 F—

<She clears her throat.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Delfina.

Saray:

 That's pretty. This place is boring.

Chief Ibanez:

 You mean the house, or the village?

Saray:

 Yeah.

<Chief Ibanez nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Then why don't you get out of here?

Saray:

 Why don't you?

<Chief Ibanez sighs.>

Saray:

 Are you hiding from someone?

Chief Ibanez:

 Not very well, apparently. Are you?

Saray:

 Nope.

Chief Ibanez:

 Any chance I can get you to hide from me, then?

Saray:

 Nope.

Chief Ibanez:

 Didn't think so.

<She walks past Saray to stand on the doorstep of the shack, looking out across the bay.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What happened to the big silo?

<Saray moves to stand beside her.>

Saray:

 What big silo? The one over there, where my mom is?

<She points to the grain silo. Dr. McDoctorate and Ursula can be seen climbing the windmill tower.>

<Chief Ibanez points across the bay.>

Chief Ibanez:

 No, on the other side, up the rise. There used to be a silo…

Saray:

 Oh! I think I know the one you mean. They took it apart a long time ago, before I was born.

Chief Ibanez:

 What did they do with it?

<Saray shrugs.>

Saray:

 Patched up the old houses, I guess. They say they were pretty beat up.

<Chief Ibanez nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 That's true. What's there now?

Saray:

 Let's go see.

<She reaches out to take Chief Ibanez's hand.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I like to keep my hands free.

Saray:

 Suit yourself.

<She skips down the path to the main road, stopping briefly to pick up a pitted green stick from the ground, taking a few practice swings.>

<Chief Ibanez watches her go.>

<She sighs.>

<She follows.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Oh.

<They are now standing on the rise on the eastern side of the bay. Where Chief Ibanez indicated the large grain silo once stood, there is a gently sloping roughly circular depression in the ground. It is filled with tall, haphazardly-arranged wooden markers; each marker bears an inscription, apparently hand-carved and then burned for additional clarity.>

<There are several hundred of them.>

Saray:

 Yeah.

<Chief Ibanez walks the gravel path between the markers. She reads the inscriptions, one after another.>

Saray:

 You know anybody?

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

Saray:

 Sorry.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

<She glances from marker to marker, but does not linger in front of any. The names Eloy, Aurelio, Ernesto, Jorge and Teresa are visible.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I wonder if they're really down there.

Saray:

 What do you mean?

<Chief Ibanez looks away from the markers, then immediately looks back and resumes reading. Saray walks beside her as she speaks.>

Chief Ibanez:

 They died in Zevala. There wasn't even enough of Eloy left to bury. And I doubt they were hauling corpses while they were hauling a—

<She looks down at the child, who looks up at her with wide eyes.>

Chief Ibanez:

 …while they were running for the Facility. Sorry.

<Saray shrugs.>

Saray:

 It doesn't matter.

Chief Ibanez:

 What doesn't matter?

Saray:

 Whether they're really buried there.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why not?

Saray:

 You don't have to be somewhere to… 

be

 somewhere. You know?

Chief Ibanez:

 No.

Saray:

 Okay.

<Chief Ibanez resumes scanning the markers. She reaches the back row, where the land starts to rise again to meet the bayside cliff, before she stops.>

Saray:

 What's wrong?

<Chief Ibanez does not respond.>

Saray:

 Delfina?

<Chief Ibanez looks away.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Nothing. It's fine.

<Saray approaches the marker Chief Ibanez was inspecting, and mouths the name to herself. She frowns, places a hand on the marker, and walks around behind it aimlessly.>

<Chief Ibanez notices the next marker, and pauses.>

Puerto Extirpado, graveyard, and SCP-8273-3.

Saray:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 Let's go.

Saray:

 But—

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm going.

<She heads for the path.>

Saray:

 It was for you?

<Chief Ibanez stops at the edge of the fence, and does not look back or respond.>

Saray:

 Guess they should pull it up.

Chief Ibanez:

 It's fine where it is.

Saray:

 But you're not—

Chief Ibanez:

 It's fine where it is.

<She leaves the graveyard. Saray runs after her, catching up easily.>

<Villagers are going about their daily tasks, hauling supplies from the caches, discussing matters with the scientists, and pointing out peculiarities in terrain to the agents. Chief Ibanez and Saray head back toward the village core.>

Saray:

 Are you an adult?

<Chief Ibanez glares at her.>

Saray:

 How come you're not much taller than me?

Chief Ibanez:

 Dunno.

Saray:

 Is the rest of your family…?

Chief Ibanez:

 No, just me. Drew the short straw, I guess.

<Saray laughs.>

Saray:

 Want to see my fort?

Chief Ibanez:

 You've got a fort?

Saray:

 Yep.

Chief Ibanez:

 Sure. Show me.

<Saray leads Chief Ibanez off the beaten path, to where a round concrete emplacement is crumbling into the lower slopes of the cliff which forms one edge of the Facility's gulch farther west. It is covered in green vines; Saray bounds up the pitted stairs, lifts the vines, and disappears inside.>

<Chief Ibanez remains outside, hands on her hips.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I was expecting a tree fort.

<Saray's face appears between the vines and the concrete.>

Saray:

 Mom says we can't climb the trees.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why not?

Saray:

 Because the trees eat people.

Chief Ibanez:

 Huh.

Saray:

 Do they eat people where you're from?

Chief Ibanez:

 No. I don't think so, anyway. Then again, there's probably…

<She considers.>

Chief Ibanez:

 No.

<She walks up the steps, lifts the vines, and enters Saray's 'fort'. The base of the Chaos Insurgency gun emplacement has crumbled away entirely, and someone has excavated the dirt below to create a sort of cistern. A variety of objects of interest to a child are scattered about. Discarded rebar can be seen, as can the holes widened around where it used to be threaded through the concrete, providing keyhole glimpses of the village.>

Saray:

 Do you know how to climb?

<Chief Ibanez sits cross-legged in the fort. Saray follows suit.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Sure. I lived in a tree for a while.

Saray:

 Really? Why?

Chief Ibanez:

 I was spying on some people.

Saray:

 Like a game?

Chief Ibanez:

 No.

Saray:

 Were they bad people?

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

<Chief Ibanez reaches up to test the elasticity of the vine ceiling, and grunts.>

Chief Ibanez:

 This is a pretty cool fort.

Saray:

 Right? Mom says it used to be a battery, but I can't see any plugs.

Chief Ibanez:

 Weird.

Saray:

 All the lights and stuff comes from batteries. I've seen them. They're shiny and small.

Chief Ibanez:

 Uh huh.

Saray:

 You know something you're not saying.

Chief Ibanez:

 How'd you figure that?

Saray:

 You're like mom and dad. You're talking the way they talk when they don't want to say anything.

Chief Ibanez:

 Mmm.

Saray:

 Just like that.

Chief Ibanez:

 You want to know something about your fort, Saray?

Saray:

 Sure.

<Chief Ibanez lifts the vines and points.>

Chief Ibanez:

 One time, I ran up that road, real fast, about where that rock is now, and I jumped, and it took me all the way from there to all the way up here. And there was a man up here, turning a big, big gun. He was going to shoot down some planes up in the sky.

Saray:

 What's a plane?

<Chief Ibanez pauses.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Like a big metal bird you can ride.

Saray:

 There's birds you can ride around here. But mom says I can't.

Chief Ibanez:

 Let me guess. They eat people?

Saray:

 Yeah. What did you do about the man?

Chief Ibanez:

 His gun had a little hole at the bottom, for putting in the big bullets. It had a thick iron door on it. I put his head in the hole, and then I shut the door.

Saray:

 All the way?

Chief Ibanez:

 Close enough.

Saray:

 Wow.

Chief Ibanez:

 That doesn't freak you out?

Saray:

 I guess he deserved it.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah, he did.

Saray:

 So that's alright then.

<Saray picks up a carved wooden model of a cargo ship, and sails it lazily through the air.>

<She glances at Chief Ibanez, and frowns.>

Saray:

 What's wrong?

Chief Ibanez:

 Nothing's wrong.

Saray:

 You're doing it again. Not talking.

Chief Ibanez:

 I don't like to talk.

<Chief Ibanez exhales loudly. Saray jumps.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Okay, actually. Maybe you're freaking me out a little bit, kid.

Saray:

 Why?

Chief Ibanez:

 You look like you weigh about twenty pounds soaking wet, and you didn't even blink when I told you I stuck a guy's head in the breech of a mortar in the middle of your fort one time. Tough as nails, aren't you?

<Saray shrugs.>

Saray:

 We have to be tough around here. It's a tough place.

<She flexes the muscles of her right arm — entirely obscured beneath the thick sweater — and growls menacingly.>

<Chief Ibanez looks away.>

Saray:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 You remind me of somebody.

Saray:

 You too.

<They sit in silence for a while. Chief Ibanez eventually looks back at Saray, and then at the toy ship. It resembles the

 Northern Reach 

in many respects.>

Saray:

 Are you going to move in with us?

<Chief Ibanez sounds surprised.>

Chief Ibanez:

 No. I've got a job to do.

Saray:

 That's what dad said. Before he left.

Chief Ibanez:

 Left?

Saray:

 He went to the winter.

Chief Ibanez:

 You mean he died.

Saray:

 No, I told you. He went to the winter.

Chief Ibanez:

 Winter isn't a place. You can't just go to winter.

Saray:

 We can. You'll see.

Chief Ibanez:

 How do you figure that?

Saray:

 You're a hero. He's probably in trouble. So you're gonna go find him.

<Chief Ibanez laughs.>

Saray:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 I was going to say I'm not a hero, but I've still got this f—

<Saray grins.>

Chief Ibanez:

 —this 

thing

 strapped to my back.

Saray:

 Can I see it?

Chief Ibanez:

 If I say 'yes', you will understand that I do not mean you can 

touch

 it?

Saray:

 Sure.

Chief Ibanez:

 Okay.

<She leans forward, to avoid damaging the vine ceiling, and draws SCP-6500-SWORD. It is glimmering faintly.>

Saray:

 Whoa. Is it magic?

Chief Ibanez:

 Matter of fact it is.

Saray:

 It glows.

Chief Ibanez:

 It does.

Saray:

 Like the flowers.

<Chief Ibanez glances around the blade at her.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You've got those here too?

Saray:

 My dad used to bring some home.

Chief Ibanez:

 From the Facility?

Saray:

 The what?

Chief Ibanez:

 The big ugly building.

Saray:

 Oh. No. I don't think so?

Chief Ibanez:

 They only grow in the cold.

Saray:

 That's what he said. But they don't grow very well. They're too small, and the wrong color, he said. He didn't know why.

Chief Ibanez:

 He tried to grow them here?

Saray:

 That's what he said.

Chief Ibanez:

 Hmm.

Saray:

 I don't even know what he wants them for. He used to give them to me and my sister.

Chief Ibanez:

 What for?

Saray:

 To put in our hair.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Who do I remind you of?

Saray:

 Who do I remind 

you

 of?

<Transcript ends.>

Shortly after the noonday meals, Chief Ibanez confronted Ursula Pelaez in the latter's home. A transcript of their conversation is appended below.

<Transcript begins.>

<Ursula is putting away the last of the dishes as Chief Ibanez storms in. Her finger is raised before she even enters the room.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You. And my dad.

<Ursula closes the upper cabinet, though there are still dishes in the sink, and sits down at the kitchen table. She gestures for Chief Ibanez to be seated as well, but the latter remains standing.>

Ursula:

 Who told you?

Chief Ibanez:

 Nobody.

<She takes a deep breath, and puffs out her cheeks before swallowing it again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Saray and Pilar?

Ursula:

 That's right.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why didn't you tell me?

Ursula:

 It's already a lot for you to process.

Chief Ibanez reaches to pull out a chair. Her fingers wrap around the top, then tighten, and her muscles constrict, and she nearly hurls it against the wall instead. She keeps her grip and stands her ground as she responds.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What's to process? The fact that you all fucked off and left me to die in a burning harbour? The fact that I thought you were all dead for thirty years?

Ursula:

 We didn't know it was you.

Chief Ibanez:

 Would it have made a difference?

Ursula:

 Of course it would have. We tried not to leave anyone behind. We searched all the prisons while the bombs were falling. We gathered everyone we could.

Chief Ibanez:

 Not me.

Ursula:

 I practically had to drag your father through the doors. He kept saying you were still out there. And his sons.

Chief Ibanez:

 I 

was

 still out there. His sons, not so much.

Ursula:

 I can't begin into imagine what you saw. What you had to do.

Chief Ibanez:

 That's too bad, because I'm not in a mood to tell you. Where's winter?

Ursula:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 Saray says her dad went to winter. Where's that?

<Ursula considers Chief Ibanez closely, lips pursed.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It's not a fucking metaphor for death, before you try that. You already misled me.

Ursula:

 I told you he was gone. He 

is

 gone.

Chief Ibanez:

 Gone 

where.

Ursula:

 Somewhere that isn't safe. A long time ago.

Chief Ibanez:

 Specify.

Ursula:

 About a month. I wasn't misleading you, Delfina. He really is gone.

Chief Ibanez:

 Did anybody tell you what I'm Chief of?

<Ursula nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 This is the only lead left that's worth pursuing. And when there's only one thing to be done, I'm gonna be the one doing it.

Ursula:

 Leave it alone. It would be a mistake to try and find him. If he hasn't come back yet, he's not going to.

Chief Ibanez:

 I wasn't intending on asking his opinion.

Ursula:

 Your people have enough to be doing right here, right now. Getting that machine ready for another trip. Getting to know your—

Chief Ibanez:

 My people are staying. This is a one-woman job.

Ursula:

 Going alone is dangerous.

<Chief Ibanez reaches over her shoulder to tap the pommel of SCP-6500-SWORD.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Now spill.

Pilar:

 I'm going with you.

<She steps forward. She had been standing past the doorway, obscured by the angle of the sun through the windows.>

<Chief Ibanez glances over her shoulder.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I remember this. Sheet metal walls don't block sound for shit.

Ursula:

 You're not going.

<Pilar approaches the table, and stands between Chief Ibanez and Ursula.>

Pilar:

 You said it yourself. She can't go alone.

Ursula:

 She can bring her wizard friends.

Chief Ibanez:

 No, they need to stay here. You were right, they've got their work and I've got mine. All of mine involves fucking shit up. I'm the only extraneous one when there's nothing needs hunting or killing.

Pilar:

 Take me, please.

Ursula:

 This is ridiculous. We don't even know where he is.

Pilar:

 I do.

<Ursula starts.>

Ursula:

 You do not.

Pilar:

 I do.

Ursula:

 How?

Pilar:

 I saw him go.

<Ursula stares at her, momentarily speechless.>

Ursula:

 And you didn't tell me.

Pilar:

 He didn't want me to.

Chief Ibanez:

 You're sure you can find it? Places change in a long time.

Pilar:

 Not this place.

Ursula:

 Pilar, no.

Pilar:

 She'll protect me.

Chief Ibanez:

 No promises.

<Pilar places a hand on Chief Ibanez's shoulder. The latter stiffens.>

Pilar:

 You'll protect me.

Chief Ibanez:

 What makes you so sure?

Pilar:

 I talked with your friends. They told me it's what you do.

<Transcript ends.>

As Pilar prepared for the journey with her mother's help, Chief Ibanez returned to Facility-34 to collect her own supplies. Dr. McDoctorate met her at the airlock.

<Transcript begins.>

<Dr. McDoctorate is already walking back into the Facility, and gesturing at Chief Ibanez to follow him. She does.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What's in your pants?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Eh?

Chief Ibanez:

 Why you so antsy?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 We've got a new problem.

Chief Ibanez:

 I was just telling someone there's nothing left here for me to do. You're not going to make a liar out of me, are you?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It's more complicated than that. I've been dealing with a bit of an issue with the TLP.

Chief Ibanez:

 What kind of an issue? And why didn't you tell me sooner?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Because you went walkabout, and anyway there's no engineering component to what went wrong. I made discreet enquiries with the locals, and they don't know anything that can help us with it.

Chief Ibanez:

 With what, exactly? I've got places to be.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 There might be less urgency than you think.

<They have reached the control chamber. Dr. McDoctorate indicates a single indicator with his left forefinger, tapping the panel for emphasis. This pages through the controls, and he hurriedly scrolls them back so that the indicator is visible again.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 This.

Chief Ibanez:

 What is it? 'RANUN'… 'RANUNCLE'…

Dr. McDoctorate:

 'RANUNCULACEAEIC ANGIOSPERMA QUOTIENT'. It's one of the tracking metrics the system uses to determine the status of its components. You'll remember it's the only one I thought seemed kind of redundant. It basically just checks whether there's plants in the hopper.

Chief Ibanez:

 Uh huh. And you know better now?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Yes. Think of it as the pilot light.

<Chief Ibanez looks at the indicator again. The readout says 'N/A'.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It's… out?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It is out.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why is it out?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Because it doesn't have enough fuel.

<Chief Ibanez exclaims noisily.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What? We've got a whole warehouse of it.

<Dr. McDoctorate makes hushing motions, and looks from side to side. Neither of his technicians is visible.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 They brought the problem to me, but they don't grok the meaning yet. It's heady. Time dilation in here isn't too bad, we only get an extra hour or two per day compared to outside—

Chief Ibanez:

 I didn't know that was still happening, either.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Yeah, well, you were playing fort, so.

Chief Ibanez:

 Smartass. Give me the bad news.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I did a test firing. The system has a mechanism for resettling the multiversal foundations, basically going for a spin without the spin, making sure everything's solid on the ground. But it's a no-go. The mechanism won't catch. It won't turn over.

Chief Ibanez:

 Don't tell me our gas went skanky between dimensions.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Skanky.

Chief Ibanez:

 You know what I mean.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'm going to keep doing tests, but at first blush? It looks like you need something other than 

Nigella cerritulus

 to get out of the places this place can get you into.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 That would have been really, really useful information to have had before we came here.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I agree, yes.

Chief Ibanez:

 And it doesn't make any fucking 

sense,

 because—

<Dr. McDoctorate raises a hand to forestall her. She swats it away, but lets him continue.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Because you flew all around the timeplane on this thing, back in the day, and you didn't need to stop at any gas stations. Yeah?

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Well, you were using the gas that was already in the tank. The plants grown hydroponically. Maybe there's something special about the growth process we don't understand.

Chief Ibanez:

 I know you checked for that, because you're not an idiot.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I would be a bad scientist if, faced with a situation where the most likely explanation is that I did something an idiot would do, I disregarded that on the basis of not thinking myself to be one.

<Chief Ibanez stares at the indicator.>

Chief Ibanez:

 So, we're stuck here.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 We might be.

Chief Ibanez:

 All right, well, keep it under your abstracted identity, alright? We don't need a panic, even if these people are supposedly professionals.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I've never heard my abstracted identity described as a hat before.

Chief Ibanez:

 In my experience, identity is something you wear.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 And wears on you?

Chief Ibanez:

 Could do.

<She turns to leave.>

<He places a hand on her shoulder.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You value that hand?

<He releases.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It's just, there is one more thing. We've been doing seismographic studies, because of the whole moving mountains thing.

Chief Ibanez:

 Okay.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I sent something to your PDA. I know you leave me on read, but you really ought to 

actually

 read this one before you go on your little walk.

Chief Ibanez:

 It's going to be a long walk, actually.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Maybe not, if you don't read the thing.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Right. Noted.

<Transcript ends.>

Addendum 8273-14, Rescue:

 The following morning, having discussed the perils of the road ahead and the best means of avoiding them, Chief Ibanez and Pilar prepared to leave Puerto Extirpado in search of Leandro Ibanez.

<Transcript begins.>

<PTF Delta-6500 and many of the villagers are gathered at the former Ibanez house. Chief Ibanez and Pilar, laden down with provisions, are standing at the mouth of the gully leading to where the cave is located in baseline reality.>

<Dr. Okorie kisses Chief Ibanez on the forehead.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Bad idea don't do this.

<Chief Ibanez pinches her. Dr. Okorie swats the top of her skull in response.>

<Dr. Astrauskas steers Dr. Okorie aside.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You don't both get to tell me—

<Dr. Astrauskas kisses her.>

Pilar:

 Oh. Okay.

<Chief Ibanez, flushed, turns away.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 At least take one of those suits.

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm not running out of power in the middle of a swamp. Appreciate the concern.

<She points at Pilar, then jerks a thumb at the entrance.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Burning greenlight.

Dr. Okorie:

 Let me come with you, god dammit!

<Chief Ibanez responds over her shoulder.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Do what we said. If I fuck this up, they're gonna need you.

<She notices Saray in the crowd, wide-eyed, and contorts her face.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm not used to kids.

Saray:

 Me either.

<Chief Ibanez attempts to say something else, then closes her mouth and simply nods. Saray nods back.>

<Chief Ibanez and Pilar head into the gully.>

Pilar:

 What was that about?

Chief Ibanez:

 Your sister's a punk.

Pilar:

 Tell me about it. But you know what I mean. What were you telling the witch?

Chief Ibanez:

 That's our word, thanks. And I was telling her she needs to protect the village if we piss anything off out here.

Pilar:

 But we're not going to piss anything off.

Chief Ibanez:

 We might.

Pilar:

 We plotted our route specifically to avoid—

<Chief Ibanez reaches over her shoulder and draws SCP-6500-SWORD. It is glowing, though only a little.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Do you know what this is?

<Pilar stares at the blade, transfixed.>

Pilar:

 Kind of. Not at all.

Chief Ibanez:

 It's a lightning rod.

<She sheathes it again, and shoulders her backpack.>

Pilar:

 What does that mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 It means that if there's anything weird out here, it's going to be attracted to us.

Pilar:

 So why did you bring it with you?

Chief Ibanez:

 Because if there's anything weird out here, it's also our best chance of getting out in one piece. Two pieces.

<They pass by a shaded copse, in the same position where Chief Ibanez's grandfather's shack once stood. There is another, lone, grave marker. They pass it by without comment.>

<Chief Ibanez jerks a thumb back at the village, now out of sight.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Was it always like that?

Pilar:

 Long as I can remember.

Chief Ibanez:

 How old are you?

Pilar:

 I don't know.

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

Pilar:

 I don't know how to explain it in a way you'll understand. Time passes differently in the World, compared to Earth. Or so they tell me.

Chief Ibanez:

 Do you know how soon after they came here you were born?

Pilar:

 Nine months by your reckoning after… a while. Maybe a year or two.

Chief Ibanez:

 How can you stand it here?

Pilar:

 Everywhere.

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

Pilar:

 This isn't here. This is everywhere. Everywhere I've ever been. Everything I've ever known. I was born and raised to stand it. Standing it is my default condition.

Chief Ibanez:

 Mm.

<They have reached the cliffside. There is a cave, farther up, as there is in baseline reality. The climb is higher, but far less steep; there are rough steps and handholds carved in the rock, allowing them to climb at relative leisure.>

Pilar:

 It must have been like that for you, at some point.

Chief Ibanez:

 What do you mean?

Pilar:

 In Zevala.

Chief Ibanez:

 No.

<They pause only briefly at the cave, which is choked with gleaming green vegetation and (according to Chief Ibanez's later verbal report) sweet-smelling. On Chief Ibanez's back, SCP-6500-SWORD thrums once with a light visible through the end of the scabbard, then returns to its low ebb.>

Chief Ibanez:

 No, Zevala was perfect, and I absolutely couldn't stand it. Couldn't wait to be out of there.

Pilar:

 Now you're talking sense.

Chief Ibanez:

 This is different. This place is a dead end.

<She walks back out of the cave mouth, and starts on the steeper trail toward the lip of the cliffs perhaps fifty feet up.>

Chief Ibanez:

 There was something beyond my village. My version of our village.

Pilar:

 There's something beyond this one too. The same things. It's just a little harder to get to.

Chief Ibanez:

 The same things, you think?

Pilar:

 Don't you see it? What the World really is?

Chief Ibanez:

 Give me some drones and satellites, maybe. Don't see the point in speculating from the ground.

Pilar:

 We're practically on the roof of everything, Delfina.

Chief Ibanez:

 Chief Ibanez. And one of these days, let me tell you what a mountain really is.

<She snorts.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Maybe I should start you on 'really tall hills', actually.

<They crest the cliff to a narrow plateau ledge, only a few more metres of rock remaining above them, and look back down on the sheltered bay. The villagers have begun dispersing back into the village. One tall figure, three smaller, and one much smaller wave at them from the top of the windmill. Pilar waves back.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You should appreciate this place while you have it.

Pilar:

 Why? You don't. And you didn't, apparently.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah. That's why.

<Above the final rise, the landscape stretches on to the fuzzy horizon. It is an expanse of trees like those in Puerto Extirpado, as seen from atop the windmill, but there is also a lower tableland leading up to a broad, algal bog which has no apparent end. Chief Ibanez and Pilar walk the tops of the cliffs, the latter leading the way to a path heading back down.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Do they ever talk about the way things were?

Pilar:

 All the time.

Chief Ibanez:

 Really?

Pilar:

 Of course. You know how they are.

Chief Ibanez:

 I know how they were.

Pilar:

 Then you know they don't change much.

Chief Ibanez:

 I guess.

Pilar:

 They used to talk about you all the time.

Chief Ibanez:

 Used to?

Pilar:

 Well, they still do from time to time. It's just that they've run out of new things to say.

Chief Ibanez:

 I could supply a few, but it's not exactly dinnertime conversation.

<In the distance, the trees sway.>

Pilar:

 I'm not a replacement.

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

<Pilar stops walking, at the edge of the cliff. The carved path to the forest floor begins a few inches from her feet.>

Pilar:

 I'm not a replacement for you.

Chief Ibanez:

 I never said you were.

Pilar:

 No, but you were thinking it. You're still thinking it.

Chief Ibanez:

 I am not.

<Chief Ibanez walks past her. Pilar follows, then walks beside her.>

Pilar:

 They didn't have me so they could forget about you.

<Chief Ibanez rolls her eyes.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Do you know why we record these conversations? Why we're both wearing cameras? It's because we're supposed to be learning things. Interesting, important things. Not these things.

Pilar:

 It's cultural. Isn't that useful to you? Meeting a new culture. Learning what they're like.

Chief Ibanez:

 You said it yourself. These people aren't new to me.

Pilar:

 Then why—

Chief Ibanez:

 —am I asking at all? Now that, that's a good question.

Pilar:

 Not what I meant. Why are you talking to me, instead of my mother, or any of the others?

Chief Ibanez:

 

Because

 I know them.

Pilar:

 And?

<The surrounding land is higher than the Puerto Extirpado table, and they have reached it already. The trees here are gnarled and overrun with glittering green ivy. A long, low hoot sounds through the forest, and Pilar starts. Chief Ibanez checks her service weapon, returns it to its holster, and keeps her hand on the butt.>

<They proceed down the path. It, too, is partially overgrown, but it can still be followed. It must have been cut back many times in the past.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You ever find a candy bar you forgot you bought? No, of course you haven't. Uh… hmm. Metaphor breakdown. You probably won't get any of my television analogies, either.

Pilar:

 Nobody I know drags things out this long.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah, the Internet's been bad for us. Don't ask me what that means. I'll just say it straight out, then: some surprises are nice. Sometimes it's nice to forget something, so you can remember it later.

Pilar:

 And this isn't one of those things.

Chief Ibanez:

 No. This is a thing I worked very, very hard to forget, to put behind me, and I'm not happy that it's in front of me again.

Pilar:

 You wish they were all dead?

<Silence on recording.>

Pilar:

 Hold up. This isn't the direction we agreed on.

<This time Chief Ibanez is the one to stop walking. She turns to face Pilar.>

Chief Ibanez:

 They 

were

 all dead. They've been dead for thirty years. I've lived almost twice as long as I knew them since they died.

Pilar:

 Say that again?

Chief Ibanez:

 I was sixteen. Those people and that place? They've been bad memories to me since before you were born. The person I am right now never met any of them. The first people 

she

 met were Chaos Insurgents, and that set the tone.

Pilar:

 You're still who you were before. Just a little different, that's all.

Chief Ibanez:

 I have nothing in common with the person they remember.

Pilar:

 Oh yeah? How long did it take them to recognize you, again?

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm a fucking dwarf.

<She turns on her heel, and resumes the trek at speed. Pilar hurries to catch up.>

Pilar:

 Were you listening? I told you, that's the wrong way.

Chief Ibanez:

 Right.

<Ahead, the trees thin out. They are heading in the direction of the bog.>

Pilar:

 No! Wrong! It's not safe.

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm just checking alternate routes.

Pilar:

 We've been over this already!

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah, well, there's a memo you didn't get.

<She scans the horizon for a moment, then nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Okay, point me the right way again.

<Pilar begins to walk back into the forest proper. Chief Ibanez grabs her arm.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Point me, I said. You're not leading. And keep well back.

<Pilar frowns, but does not argue.>

<They walk for several minutes in silence, Chief Ibanez keeping well ahead of Pilar. The path is still visible, though there are strange warps evident in the landscape which make traversal difficult at stages.>

Pilar:

 Your sword is—

Chief Ibanez:

 I'll bet.

<There is a slight tremor. Chief Ibanez stops.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I hear these didn't used to be so frequent.

Pilar:

 You think our world is ending too?

<Chief Ibanez shoots a look over her shoulder.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I specifically told my people to ixnay on the orld ending way.

<Pilar blinks.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I told them not to tell you about that.

Pilar:

 They didn't. You guys just make so many cryptic statements and exchange so many meaningful looks at poignant moments, it's hard not to notice. You know we can see and hear you, right?

<Chief Ibanez laughs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Well, don't worry about that right now. No, I don't think this world is ending. I think it's got more to do with the reason all the predators in this place are birds or trees or whatever.

Pilar:

 Trees?

Chief Ibanez:

 Saray said the trees eat people.

Pilar:

 Did she also tell you she fought a troll in the cave?

Chief Ibanez:

 No…

Pilar:

 Good, because there's no trolls in the cave, and the trees don't eat people.

Chief Ibanez:

 They sure act like they do.

Pilar:

 The waving? It's probably just the w—

<There is a violent CRACK from the earth, and the path just ahead jerks upward.>

<Chief Ibanez turns to face Pilar, and walks toward her. She raises a finger to her lips.>

<They walk back the way they came.>

<There is a much louder CRACK, and dirt falls from the sky all around them.>

<Chief Ibanez grabs Pilar by the arm, and pulls her into a run.>

<The forest erupts around them in linear features, rippling and shedding the tree cover, filling the air with the sound of snapping trunks and branches. It is difficult for the women to keep their feet as they flee.>

<SCP-6500-SWORD is apparently glowing enough for halation to appear on both camera feeds, although it is situated well behind the lenses.>

Pilar:

 …what…

Chief Ibanez:

 Save oxygen.

<She reaches down to her belt, makes a sudden motion, and then throws something to the right, hard. There is a loud BANG; she has apparently deployed a concussion grenade. The path of the landscape alterations turns to follow the noise.>

<A particularly gnarled tree is visible ahead and to the left, and Chief Ibanez steers Pilar toward it. Before the other woman can respond, Chief Ibanez has boosted her into the lower branches. Pilar scrambles up, and Chief Ibanez follows.>

<The two of them wait as the ground near the grenade's landing point continues to crack and rise. After a few minutes, during which a large pit forms and many trees fall in, long and tangled roots keeping them horizontal on the edge, the rumbling stops and the disturbances move away in the direction the women were originally heading.>

<Pilar struggles for several seconds to catch her breath. Chief Ibanez waits patiently.>

Pilar:

 What?

<Chief Ibanez hops down from the tree.>

Pilar:

 What was that?

Chief Ibanez:

 I like to think it was a reminder not to leave mad scientists on read.

<She heads in the direction of the bog again. Pilar carefully climbs down and rushes after her.>

Pilar:

 Explain that explanation?

<Chief Ibanez and Pilar are standing at the treeline again. The bog has apparently not been disturbed.>

Pilar:

 Everyone who's ever walked into that has 

died.

<Chief Ibanez nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You know what that means?

Pilar:

 Our people are careful. Too careful. They never take risks. If they die when they go in there, it means there's something in there that 

kills

 them.

Chief Ibanez:

 Right.

Pilar:

 So why is that better than getting earthquaked to death?

<Chief Ibanez does not respond. She waits.>

Pilar:

 What?

<Silence on recording.>

Pilar:

 You think… it's the same thing?

<Chief Ibanez nods.>

<Pilar sits down on the forest floor.>

Pilar:

 That would make it pretty… pretty big.

Chief Ibanez:

 Did they not teach you any swear words?

Pilar:

 So you think it moved off.

Chief Ibanez:

 We saw it move off.

Pilar:

 You knew it was down there? You intentionally stirred it up?

Chief Ibanez:

 I 

suspected

 something was down there. Only explanation for the lack of land predators in a verdant paradise. I didn't know what direction it was in. Now I do.

Pilar:

 And what if there's more than one?

Chief Ibanez:

 Don't be ridiculous. Anything that huge would have to be carnivorous.

<Chief Ibanez draws SCP-6500-SWORD.>

Chief Ibanez:

 There's definitely more than one.

Pilar:

 Why don't they go into the village?

<Chief Ibanez widens her eyes, opens her mouth and leans forward, head shaking expectantly.>

Pilar:

 Because…

<She draws a sharp breath.>

Pilar:

 …because we're severed?

Chief Ibanez:

 Right. And my friends aren't.

Pilar:

 But you are.

<Chief Ibanez ignores her.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Point is, unless there's lots of meat underground, these things probably eat each other. But we'll do in a pinch.

Pilar:

 It's probably harder to track us through a swamp.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah, it'll be an advantage for sure. As long as it's less than four feet deep.

<Pilar frowns.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Anything in there that catches wind is bound to follow me to wherever your dad is hiding.

Pilar:

 Our dad. But why? We're small fries, if it's that big. Not even morsels.

Chief Ibanez:

 Because of the sword.

<She brandishes SCP-6500-SWORD. It is glowing faintly from the earlier encounter.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It re-energizes things. Makes things happen.

Pilar:

 What sort of things?

Chief Ibanez:

 The exciting sort.

Pilar:

 So why did you bring it, if it's just going to make things harder?

Chief Ibanez:

 Because I'm the best at handling hard things. Shut up.

<Pilar looks confused.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Wow. We need to get your out more. Anyway, it's not the worst possible situation. If this stuff doesn't chase me out into the boonies, it might wander into the village. I'll bet it can smell Udo and Roz's magic and McDoctorate's ridiculous cologne on the wind.

Pilar:

 Is that his actual name? It can't be, right?

Chief Ibanez:

 So, here's what's going to happen. You're going to go climb a tree and be mouse-quiet for a bit — mice are… just be quiet, okay, and I'm going go scout the bog.

Pilar:

 How?

<Chief Ibanez sets down her backpack, and produces a small LIDAR drone and a pair of binoculars.>

Chief Ibanez:

 If it's safe, it's safe. If it's not, it will be before I come back to find you.

Pilar:

 Find me 

nothing.

 I'm coming with.

Chief Ibanez:

 Like hell you are. I need someone to catch me on camera.

Pilar:

 Doing what?

Chief Ibanez:

 Whatever it takes.

Pilar:

 What's wrong with your own camera?

<Chief Ibanez grins.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It's probably going to be moving around a lot.

<Chief Ibanez finishes her LIDAR survey of the bog, revealing it to be relatively shallow and resting on a bedrock lattice providing ample footing. She examines the results carefully, committing the landscape to memory, then proceeds in the rough direction of their destination as indicated by Pilar.>

<She moves through the water for approximately ten minutes, never submerged below the top of her waterproof boots. She holds SCP-6500-SWORD in front of her, and its soft glow does not ebb.>

<There is a sudden eruption of water and soil.>

<The next thirteen minutes of footage come from Pilar's body camera. All footage from Chief Ibanez is blurred and obscured to the point of incomprehensibility; Pilar's footage is zoomed in to 4000% to accommodate the distance between lens and subject, rendering everything extremely low-fidelity and subject to considerable motion blurring.>

<Chief Ibanez subsequently provided additional information regarding the events described below and her actions during them, which have been interpolated where appropriate.>

<The water of the bog has been broken by a tremendous spined form stretching from Chief Ibanez's position to at least several hundred metres away. It begins thrashing, and algae and mud fill the air. Chief Ibanez leaps from her starting position to the nearest bedrock protrusion, and an enormous club-shaped tail pulverizes the space she has just been occupying. She raises SCP-6500-SWORD and shouts: "¡En guardia!">

.

Audible on recording only as a distant, incoherent shriek.

<Footage is briefly obscured as Pilar hurriedly climbs a tree and secrets herself among the branches. She is able to achieve a vantage point between the broad leaves, revealing the scene again. The bog is already unrecognizable, with a massive pit filling with swamp water; the tail is slamming down again and again, tearing deep divots into the bedrock and excavating the soil down to the peat layer. Chief Ibanez is leaping from rock to rock around the rim of the pit, waving SCP-6500-SWORD defensively. A tremendous ribbed space resembling a cave has risen in front of her, filled with what appear to be stalactites and stalagmites.

.

Chief Ibanez has confirmed that this was in fact the maw of a living creature.

 It recoils from the sword, with geological import; the tree in which Pilar is situated shakes.>

<A massive forelimb emerges from the bog, with talons significantly larger than Chief Ibanez, and they rake the air. Chief Ibanez swings SCP-6500-SWORD, colliding with the longest talon and shattering it with a tremendous burst of air which entirely denudes Pilar's trees of leaves two seconds later. Chief Ibanez is hurled away, landing in the water on her back. She still has hold of SCP-6500-SWORD. She is underwater for only an instant, spluttering back to the surface and swimming for the nearest surviving crop of bedrock. She spits up the last of the water and yells: "Fuck this!">

.

Inaudible; recording is dominated by a deep bestial groan.

<The creature's back is emerging from the bog, metre by metre. There are ripples in its pebbled flesh, and it shudders, and two wings on the approximate scale of a Boeing B-52 Stratofortress rise from the water and begin to spread. A moment later the creature bucks forward, and a second pair of wings extends perhaps one hundred metres back. Chief Ibanez sinks to a runner's crouch, and roars at the creature defiantly. It becomes possible to discern the creature's neck as it extends its vast mouth toward Chief Ibanez, who is pointing a brightly-glowing SCP-6500-SWORD at it, and roars back with enough force to send her reeling. It then makes purchase on the bedrock with its talons, and begins drawing its full body out of the water.>

<Chief Ibanez states, at this point: "Finally.">

.

Inaudible; Pilar is screaming.

<Chief Ibanez charges the creature, still roaring.>

<A shower of water from the altercation belatedly falls onto Pilar, drenching her.>

Chief Ibanez engaged in combat, representative frame.

<The next twenty-one seconds are difficult to discern visually, but Chief Ibanez's subsequent commentary tracks with what is visible. The creature, in roaring, has placed Chief Ibanez at eye level — the segmentations of its hide become iridescent in patches near the top of its head, and these are presumed to be its eyes. It turns its head to one side, presumably to examine Chief Ibanez in birdlike fashion; she thrusts SCP-6500-SWORD in its direction, and a massive burst of light strikes the eye-scales, and the creature reels back in surprise. Chief Ibanez presses the attack, dislodging a scale from the creature's right forelimb and gaining purchase there with the slick treads of her combat boots. Stabbing at the creature's hide to create additional purchases, she makes her way up its trunk as it attempts to locate the source of its new injuries.>

<The creature leaps into the air, leaving the bog entirely. Chief Ibanez has affixed climbing pitons to the holes in the creature's scale cover, and has secured herself to them with SCP-6500-SWORD's harness. The creature roars again, this time so loud that Pilar falls out of the tree, screaming. Her landing is softened by the now-sodden ground, but her camera lens is obscured.>

<Sounds of scrabbling, screaming, roaring, crashing, and splashing occupy the next four minutes and forty-seven seconds of both recordings. Chief Ibanez's full accounting of her actions at this time is on record with RAISA.>

<As the sound subsides, save for a series of tremendous thunderclaps Chief Ibanez will later identify as the beating of six sets of wings, her camera view finally stabilizes. The creature has already almost vanished into the murky horizon, with only a silhouette discernible.>

<She makes her way slowly back to the shore, panting and coughing. The trees on the forest edge look blasted; Pilar is slumped with her back to the tree she had climbed, and she is staring at Chief Ibanez with wild eyes.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Tell me you got some of that.

<Pilar screams.>

<After an interval of approximately fourteen minutes, during which neither woman speaks, Chief Ibanez has attended to minor abrasions on her skin while Pilar's camera has been cleaned and checked for damage. Chief Ibanez is seen to be soaked from head to toe, but save for some fraying on the cuffs and divots in the armour from ascending the razor-sharp scales, her combat uniform is largely intact.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Hahaha.

Pilar:

 How.

<Chief Ibanez shrugs, and climbs to her feet.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I want to say the sword did it.

<SCP-6500-SWORD, having been employed multiple times in the altercation, now glows only dimly.>

Pilar:

 But?

Chief Ibanez:

 Talk to Place. I'm all out of hot air.

<She reaches down to help Pilar up, an operation made slightly awkward by the foot in difference between their heights. The taller woman stands, shakily, and expels a loud sigh.>

Pilar:

 I don't know what to say.

Chief Ibanez:

 Best possible result.

<She shoulders her gear, and begins the descent down the ruined shoreline to the bog.>

Pilar:

 Did you kill it?

Chief Ibanez:

 No.

Pilar:

 What if it comes back?

Chief Ibanez:

 I'll have caught my breath, assuming you don't make me waste any talking.

Pilar:

 What if it heads for the village instead?

Chief Ibanez:

 It won't. But if it does—

<She has raised a hand to forestall Pilar's objection.>

Chief Ibanez:

 —Udo can pick up half the bay and flense the fucker to the dinosaur bone. It's not the only thing around here that can move mountains.

<Pilar's eyes widen.>

Pilar:

 I'd like to see that.

Chief Ibanez:

 Honestly? So would I.

<The trek through the bog is slow; though the water is not deep, thick layers of mud are built up over the bedrock lattice, much of it churned up by the creature's passage and emergence. It takes several hours to reach a patch of solid ground above the water table identified by Chief Ibanez's drone survey, and as the task is unpleasant both women are largely silent for the duration.>

<The sky is a dark green by the time they reach the island, and the spores are fluorescing thick and early. Chief Ibanez sets up a portable fire kit and a pair of bedrolls, though the night air is warm.>

Pilar:

 You should have brought the dragon over here.

<Chief Ibanez arches a brow.>

Pilar:

 I'll bet it burns better than soggy old wood.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why would it burn at all?

Pilar:

 Did you smell it?

<Chief Ibanez's eyes widen.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I was trying not to inhale.

Pilar:

 Well, it smelled like peat. It was under a peat bog. I think it was 

made

 of peat, and that stuff burns really well.

Chief Ibanez:

 Huh.

Pilar:

 Yeah.

<Silence on recording.>

<Chief Ibanez bursts into laughter, and slaps her thigh. Pilar jumps.>

Pilar:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 Peat dragon. 

Peat's Dragon.

<Pilar blinks.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Never mind.

<She shivers lightly, and rolls her jumpsuit sleeves back down.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Bit nippy now. What are the seasons here?

Pilar:

 What's a season?

<Silence on recording.>

<Pilar laughs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Fuck you.

<She laughs as well.>

Pilar:

 But it would have been a fair statement. I've just heard stories. Snow sounds interesting.

Chief Ibanez:

 The fucking Canadians think it makes them special. They act like they're born to it. Northern people, hardy and wind-whipped. Load of horse shit.

<There is a single dead tree on the island, and Chief Ibanez is able to find enough dry branches to start a fire. She begins setting up her portable cooking equipment.>

Pilar:

 What if something out here is attracted to fire?

Chief Ibanez:

 Then the sword would call them anyway. And the sword will take care of them.

<Pilar watches Chief Ibanez pour a can of stew into a small bowl, and cook it over the fire. The can bears the emblem of the Secure Containment Institute.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Soup from a dead timeline, cooked in an alternate universe, eaten by people from two different realities. Globalism is out of control.

<Pilar has been looking at the pommel of SCP-6500-SWORD since Chief Ibanez mentioned it.>

Pilar:

 You must be pretty important to have a weapon like that.

Chief Ibanez:

 It's not mine.

Pilar:

 No?

Chief Ibanez:

 Actually, you know what? It 

is

 mine. I found it, and I powered it up. I saved the interesting parts of the world with it.

Pilar:

 And now you're saving us.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

Pilar:

 You don't seem too excited about it.

<Chief Ibanez stirs the stew.>

Pilar:

 It doesn't require that much attention.

Chief Ibanez:

 We'll introduce you to more people on the other side. You'll learn social cues, like when someone doesn't want to pursue a conversational topic.

Pilar:

 All those people you know never taught you when someone's not taking 'no' for an answer.

<Chief Ibanez sits back on her haunches, and watches the stew bubble.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Do you know what Florence is?

Pilar:

 No.

Chief Ibanez:

 Italy?

Pilar:

 Vaguely.

Chief Ibanez:

 Florence is a city in Italy. It has a cathedral. Do—

Pilar:

 I know what a cathedral is.

Chief Ibanez:

 It took like a hundred years to build this thing. The original architect died, and nobody could figure out how to put a roof on it. Biggest roof they'd ever had to make, bigger than the world had seen since back when they had slaves and dictators.

<She frowns.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Well, they still… no, finish the story. If you showed that dead old architect the finished product, he wouldn't have recognized it. I'm sure it wasn't what he imagined. Some new guy came along and had all the right ideas for finishing up that roof, decades later, and it made the whole thing one of the most famous buildings in the world. That first guy? He had an idea. The second guy? He had a plan, and he made it happen.

Pilar:

 Okay.

Chief Ibanez:

 When something's big and complex enough, and it takes decades to put together, you only get full credit for it when you're around to see it through. If you're not, it's left to other people. And the results belong as much to them. Maybe more. Probably more. Anybody can doodle on a napkin, Pilar.

Pilar:

 But buildings aren't people.

Chief Ibanez:

 You're right. People start building themselves, from an early stage. The people who are there with you while you're doing that? They matter. They matter a lot. The people who aren't?

<Silence on recording.>

Pilar:

 They were there at the start. Like the architect. They put in a lot of work. A lot of love, before they had to leave.

Chief Ibanez:

 Difference is, the architect had no choice. Stew's ready.

<Both women deactivate their cameras during the night, reactivating shortly after first light. They pack up their equipment in the morning, and Chief Ibanez briefly checks in with the Foundation personnel back in Puerto Extirpado by radio before setting out again with Pilar.>

<The second leg of the journey is less difficult; the spaces between the bedrock lattice are smaller, and easier to see even without the survey data, and the water is clearer as well.>

Pilar:

 I don't understand bogs.

Chief Ibanez:

 Me either, but this isn't one.

Pilar:

 What do you mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 Bogs aren't mud stuck through a honeycomb of rock. Whatever these formations are, they're not natural. Paranatural, maybe.

Pilar:

 What does 

that

 mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 It means your proto-world is weirder than my full one, in a few respects. Not as well-populated with bizarreness, but give it time.

Pilar:

 You think this place is in an earlier stage of evolution?

Chief Ibanez:

 I think I'd rather leave that question to the people who really care about it.

<They walk for two more hours, and a gradual atmospheric change takes place. The air is less warm now, and the water is very still. There are spores on the air again, but they are white and blue instead of green, in spite of the sky. It is not uncomfortably cool, and they cannot see their breath, but the climatic trend is definitely downward.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Going to winter, huh.

Pilar:

 Feels like it shouldn't transition this fast.

Chief Ibanez:

 It definitely shouldn't. Could be the world's still settling into its shoes. Or, might be magic.

<Pilar laughs, then sees the look on Chief Ibanez's face.>

Pilar:

 I keep forgetting magic is real.

Chief Ibanez:

 That's what happens when your beliefs are challenged. Your brain tries to fit the new information into the space where the old used to fit, only there isn't enough room, and the old just fits so 

well.

 It's a coping mechanism.

Pilar:

 You adapted pretty well to all the changes.

Chief Ibanez:

 Do you know how exercise works?

<Pilar sighs.>

Pilar:

 Can you just say what you mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 The only way to make something more flexible is to bend and twist until it breaks a bit, and then knit it all back stronger. Is that…?

<In the far distance, the bog ends on what looks to be a rocky shore. In the distance, very faintly, a rectilinear feature is visible.>

Pilar:

 I've never been there.

Chief Ibanez:

 But that's it, right? That's where…

Pilar:

 Where he went? I think so.

<It takes another half hour to escape the final reaches of the bog and clamber up the stones, then dry off their gear and approach the cabin. The construction is even more crude than that of the villages in Puerto Extirpado, and it is smaller as well. The metal is rusted through in many places, though thick sheets have been hung on the inside to block the flow of cool air. There is a rack for hanging clothes to dry by the near wall, and a cooking pit on the other side. Out front there is a wheelbarrow, its components carved from green wood, with a broken wheel. Tools are piled beside it on the earth, as though discarded in frustration. There is a long bench and a rickety chair, both constructed from the same material. A jerry can lies on its side beside the bench, cap absent. >

<The two women stop just before the front door. Pilar speaks, very quietly.>

Pilar:

 I'll go first.

<Chief Ibanez visibly strains to step forward and overtake her, but her feet do not move. Pilar opens the shack door.>

Pilar:

 Dad?

<The shack interior is indifferently kept. Rusted agricultural tools are tossed here and there on the hardpacked floor. There are opened cans in the primitive sink, and the bed is unmade. A gaunt older man in a badly-patched hooded sweater and jeans is sitting crosslegged on the floor, repairing an old shirt with needle and thread. He is staring at Pilar in shock.>

Leandro:

 What the hell are you doing out here?! It isn't safe!

<He puts the shirt aside and stands, moving quickly across the small space to embrace his daughter.>

Pilar:

 It's safer than it was.
