SCP-8273-1.

Addendum 8273-15, Return:

 Leandro suggested remaining at the cabin until the next morning, but Chief Ibanez demurred, citing the fact that a safe path through the bog had now been determined and the return journey would not take longer than the remainder of the day. Leandro accepted this decision, but insisted on a brief detour half an hour's walk from the cabin first.

<Transcript begins.>

<Leandro leads at a distance across the increasingly-frozen terrain. Ice on the ground glistens with unnatural brightness. Chief Ibanez and Pilar speak in low tones as they proceed. If Leandro is listening, he gives no indication.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm still not clear on how you knew where to go.

Pilar:

 Hmm?

Chief Ibanez:

 Don't fucking 

hmm

 me. I'm the Chief of Pursuit and Suppression, your evasiveness is doomed from the start.

Pilar:

 I was just—

Chief Ibanez:

 Stalling to come up with an excuse, yeah, I know. Too bad. This place is almost impossible to map, and I get the distinct impression you've never actually been here before.

Pilar:

 Yeah, well.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah? Well?

<Pilar reaches into the back pocket of her jeans, and hands Chief Ibanez a water-damaged paper map. It is drawn in a child's hand.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Saray.

Pilar:

 Yeah. She saw him go, and snuck after him. He made her promise not to tell.

Chief Ibanez:

 How'd you get her to?

Pilar:

 I didn't. She came to me.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why?

<She pauses.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Because she knew I could save him?

Pilar:

 No, because she knew you needed to.

Chief Ibanez:

 I do like that kid.

<She shakes her head ruefully.>

Pilar:

 Are you going to forgive him?

<Leandro looks at the ground. A slight but very broad depression in the earth is now visible ahead.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It doesn't matter.

Pilar:

 Of course it matters.

Chief Ibanez:

 Sorry, I was doing the thing again.

Pilar:

 What thing?

Chief Ibanez:

 Overcomplication. What I meant to say was it's none of your fucking business.

<Pilar smiles.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

Pilar:

 You wouldn't be this angry if it didn't still matter to you.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Why not just give me the map, though?

Pilar:

 Hmm?

Chief Ibanez:

 Why come with?

Pilar:

 You're not the only one who's ever wanted to leave home, Chief.

<Chief Ibanez nods, seems to consider something, then nods again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You can call me Delfina.

<Leandro looks back at them.>

Leandro:

 We're here.

<He is standing at the edge of the depression, which slopes down further into a shallow valley a few metres on . The valley is filled with blackened soil, and the mummified remains of unusual vegetation.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What is this?

Leandro:

 The ashes of our last hope.

Chief Ibanez:

 Less flowery?

Leandro:

 No, that's just it. That's what this is.

<Chief Ibanez walks past him to examine the vegetation more clearly. She picks up one of the stalks, and sucks a breath in through her teeth.>

Leandro:

 This is my 

Nigella

 plantation.

<Chief Ibanez mutters the next sentence under her breath.>

Chief Ibanez:

 No leylines for miles, she said.

Leandro:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 Nothing. What's it doing way the hell out here?

Leandro:

 Same thing the cabin is. Been here for generations. The flowers too. Waiting for us to return.

Chief Ibanez:

 And only you knew where it was? Before now?

Leandro:

 The men tend the flowers, and maintain the machine. The women have the visions, and make the decisions.

Chief Ibanez:

 Nursery rhyme sexism. I guess it's nice to have a mnemonic.

Pilar:

 What happened to them? The flowers, I mean.

Leandro:

 Wouldn't grow. Rotted so badly they scorched the permafrost. All that potential energy had to go somewhere.

<He shrugs. The gesture seems forced.>

Leandro:

 I guess it's possible to be too much a stranger.

Chief Ibanez:

 You planted them?

Leandro:

 I did. That's why I came out here, the first time. When we arrived. I wanted to grow a new crop, so that…

Pilar:

 …you could go looking for her?

Chief Ibanez:

 So he could get out of this lime-green hellhole.

Leandro:

 Whatever you want to believe.

<Leandro slouches in a posture of defeat.>

Leandro:

 I thought I understood the principles. As usual, I was wrong. It takes years for these things to grow, you know. They should have been ready by now. Instead…

Chief Ibanez:

 That's why you didn't go back. To Puerto Extirpado.

Leandro:

 They're better off without me.

Pilar:

 That's not true.

<Chief Ibanez rotates the desiccated stalk in her fingertips, thoughtfully.>

Leandro:

 I just… I hoped it would work. But hope isn't always enough.

Pilar:

 But it's fine, right? We don't need them.

Chief Ibanez:

 Sure. It's fine.

<She stands, dropping the stem to the ashen earth. Pilar's camera captures the last of the light from SCP-6500-SWORD sputtering out.>

<Transcript ends.>

Chief Ibanez, Pilar and Leandro reached Puerto Extirpado at approximately midnight, after an uneventful trek through the bog, forest, and hills. Chief Ibanez radioed ahead; a party met them where the gully opened on the rear of the abandoned Ibanez shack.

<Transcript begins.>

<Drs. Astrauskas, McDoctorate and Okorie, Ursula and Saray are waiting at the shack when Chief Ibanez emerges. She steps aside to let Leandro pass; he moves tentatively into the village proper, and is immediately pounced upon by his younger daughter.>

Leandro:

 Little fish.

<He kneels to embrace her, and they remain that way in silence while the others speak.>

<Pilar hugs her mother.>

Pilar:

 Told you we'd be fine.

<Ursula draws back, and brushes a few specks of muck from Pilar's face and hair.>

Ursula:

 You don't look fine.

Chief Ibanez:

 Nothing a bath won't fix.

<Seeing Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie approach her, Chief Ibanez adopts a hostile posture.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I think she thinks we're going to kiss her again.

Dr. Okorie:

 Well, I was.

<Ursula approaches Leandro, a sorrowful smile on her face. He stands — Saray remains attached to his legs — and allows her to embrace him as well.>

Leandro:

 I'm sorry.

Ursula:

 Hush.

Leandro:

 I tried—

Ursula:

 Hush, I said.

<Dr. Okorie kneels to examine the damage to Chief Ibanez's uniform.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Are you okay?

Chief Ibanez:

 Obviously.

Dr. Okorie:

 I don't mean—

Chief Ibanez:

 I need to talk to Place. Anything to report before I do?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Nothing that can't wait.

Chief Ibanez:

 Good.

<She stalks off, in the general direction of Facility-34.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Are you gonna catch one of those showers?

Chief Ibanez:

 Might be a waste of time.

<When she has disappeared beyond the edge of the shack, Dr. Okorie turns to see Leandro staring at her. Ursula is fussing over the state of his clothing, silently.>

Leandro:

 Hello.

Dr. Okorie:

 Mr. Ibanez?

Leandro:

 I go by Pelaez.

Dr. Okorie:

 Is that your first name?

Leandro:

 No, it…

<He frowns.>

Leandro:

 Fina never told you my…?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 She speaks. But she speaks slowly.

Dr. Okorie:

 Some sentences take years.

Leandro:

 You're her…

<Leandro gestures at the rings on their fingers.>

Dr. Okorie:

 That's right.

Ursula:

 It's good.

<He glances at her, uncertain.>

Leandro:

 It's good?

Ursula:

 Yes.

<He keeps eye contact for a moment, nods, and looks back at Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie.>

Leandro:

 Well. Good. Pleased to meet you.

<He extends a hand, and each woman shakes it in turn.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Likewise.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I think we've all got a lot to talk about.

Leandro:

 I've told Fina everything I know.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Mmm.

<Her eyes are narrowed.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You shouldn't feel bad she didn't tell us about you, Mr. Pelaez.

<He gives her an inquisitive look.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Because apparently she didn't tell you about me, either.

<Transcript ends.>

Chief Ibanez consulted briefly with Dr. McDoctorate, confirming that the state of the Trans-Liminal Propulser was no better than before. She passed on her information regarding the failed 

Nigella

 crop, and was in the process of workshopping a possible solution to the dilemma when Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie joined them in the control room.

<Transcript begins.>

<Both Dr. Astrauskas and Dr. Okorie are carrying data tablets filled with the information they have gleaned both from and about the locals during Chief Ibanez's absence.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You've got good news.

Dr. Okorie:

 How can you tell?

Chief Ibanez:

 That wasn't speculation. That was an order.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Well, I don't know if this counts as 

good,

 particularly, but it's interesting at least. I think the severing really is what they say it is. There's Hume tendrils waving off every one of the Extirpadans, stopping just short of each other, shearing every which way. You've got them too, and they've been reaching out ever since we arrived. I noticed it as soon as we found Pilar in the gulch. That's what I was going to tell you at the town hall.

<She waves in the air, tracing lines only she can see. Chief Ibanez follows the trail of her fingertips, looking uneasy.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 They've also all got the same declension you have.

Chief Ibanez:

 And what do you think that means?

Dr. Okorie:

 Could it just be because they're from Aph? Originally?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 No. The Aphians have a slight Hume 

elevation.

 This is on the other side of baseline.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I have an idea.

Chief Ibanez:

 About how we can get out of here?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'm still working on that. Did you think I'd forgotten?

Chief Ibanez:

 You're a mad scientist. It was at least worth considering.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Mad science is just something you perform. It's not an identity.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Have you met Everett Mann?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 The point is, I'm not comfortable talking about that subject on the record.

Dr. Okorie:

 Why?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I'm not comfortable explaining why on the record, either.

<Chief Ibanez kicks the base of the nearest console, and the metal vibrates loudly. They all turn to face her.>

Chief Ibanez:

 We're learning a lot about everyone's comfort zones. That's great. Now finish explaining the stupid Hume thing.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Personally, I think it's a consequence of dimensional travel. Not an indicator of origin, but repeated transportation.

Chief Ibanez:

 How would that work?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Do you know how the transporters on 

Star Trek

 function?

<Dr. Astrauskas winces.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 If that's the explanation, don't explain it.

Chief Ibanez:

 What? What's he talking about?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Never you mind. But that would certainly explain the discrepancies. Not that we could have known it before we figured out what the machine does.

Chief Ibanez:

 I think that's why the TAD fucked with my old file, too. They didn't want anyone realizing this place existed outside of time.

Dr. Okorie:

 Probably they would have wanted something like that for themselves.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 They have something like that for themselves.

<The others turn to look at him.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 You ever been debriefed by them? Don't recommend it.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You remember everything now, right?

Chief Ibanez:

 Now, in this moment, in this room, yes.

Dr. Okorie:

 I still don't understand why your memories were location-specific. Has anyone been forgetting what they've learned in Puerto Extirpado?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 No, because I properly fixed those exchangers.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What did they exchange?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Psychic fields. Those first dimensional travellers all died because the systems didn't properly sort their memory sets between worlds. Every one of their possible selves tried to template on the same brains, and fried them. The caretakers must have understood the machinery just well enough to jury-rig a stopgap system that compartmentalized you between each reality. Me, I like to work from first principles.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why didn't it do that to the Prophets? The diary says they all lived, only the Institute people kicked off.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Best guess? The Prophets don't have alternate selves.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I don't know why, but I don't like the sound of that.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I do know why. You're happier not knowing.

Chief Ibanez:

 Getting a bit tired of hearing that.

Dr. Okorie:

 So, okay. Memories compartmentalized to each universe, before, but not anymore? Meaning if we went back to all the other places Del visited…

Dr. McDoctorate:

 …she'd get to keep her memories once she reclaimed them, yes.

Chief Ibanez:

 Pass.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Let's get back to the memories at hand. The journal entries are undated. How long were you in here for, really? Well, not really. Subjectively.

Chief Ibanez:

 Maybe two years.

Dr. Okorie:

 What?!

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I thought it was months at the outside. Jesus Christ.

Chief Ibanez:

 Think about it. When I came in, I was an angry teenager on a lucky streak. I came out in military power armour with the mental and physical capability to use it. I came out with enough engineering knowledge for a Foundation degree. Muscle mass you'd usually need steroids to get. This place gave me all the time I needed to make myself into something new.

<She sighs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 And last week, when I stepped outside again for the first time, I remembered green hell too. Not just what was in the journals, all of it. It was different when I first visited; wilder, more dangerous, no village. That's where I taught myself how to use the suit.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Just popping around the corner and back a few times shouldn't have been enough to affect your Hume spirals so dramatically.

Chief Ibanez:

 It wasn't. I went to lots of other places. More than I wrote about. I wasn't a big writer. And like I said, emptied out the hydroponics.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You went on a multidimensional training voyage.

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Like—

Chief Ibanez:

 Like some batshit version of Batman.

Dr. Okorie:

 Sheesh.

Chief Ibanez:

 Aphora will be jealous.

<Dr. Astrauskas is nodding.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Yeah, that's it. That's what I saw.

Dr. Okorie:

 How can you tell?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Because now that I know to look, I can see that all of our Hume spirals are slightly off too.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 By how much?

<She indicates with her forefinger and thumb.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Tiny little fraction.

Dr. Okorie:

 Compared to Del's?

<She squints.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Hard to say. I've got a point scale, but it's more subjective than anything. Maybe a tenth? Maybe a twentieth.

Dr. Okorie:

 Holy shit.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 And here I thought we all took our first multidimensional trip together.

Chief Ibanez:

 Well, don't feel bad. We've probably taken our last one together.

Dr. Okorie:

 What's that mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 Egghead says our flowers won't work on this side.

Dr. Okorie:

 Kept that to yourself, did you?

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm the commander. That's my job.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Well, you should have shared the job.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Because the villagers were talking about this already, obviously. They said they couldn't get the mechanism to work either, so they were really surprised when you pulled the Facility back to baseline. They thought somebody had figured out how to use it again, and abandoned them.

Chief Ibanez:

 Somebody.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Yes. Your father.

Chief Ibanez:

 Figures. But that's not really useful information, is it?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It is if I'm reading the implications correctly. I think your father knows something the rest of them don't. And if I'm right, we might be able to get out of here after all.

Chief Ibanez:

 Well, spill the beans.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 First I need to see if I can get the beans to spill.

Chief Ibanez:

 What the hell does that mean?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I get to have secrets too. This is an equitable relationship we're in.

<Dr. Okorie and Chief Ibanez emerge from the Facility together.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What were you talking to Place about before we came in?

Chief Ibanez:

 Stranger-in-the-Mist needs leyline proximity to grow, is that right?

<Dr. Okorie nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 That's what the demonics were for, in the hydroponics, you figure?

<Dr. Okorie nods again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Are there any leylines 

here?

 In this world?

Dr. Okorie:

 There are not. Not for hundreds of miles in every direction.

Chief Ibanez:

 How do you know?

Dr. Okorie:

 I set up a skein under the ground, put out feelers as far as I could go without using myself. Roz read my aura while I was doing it. New thing we figured out, I did send you the paper a few months back.

Chief Ibanez:

 Well, you knew what that would get you.

Dr. Okorie:

 Hope springs eternal.

Chief Ibanez:

 So everyone keeps telling me.

Dr. Okorie:

 You're wondering if it's possible to grow the plants here?

Chief Ibanez:

 No, just musing. Can a leyline be alive?

<Dr. Okorie blinks.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Leylines are magical conduits in the earth. The demonics are a dirty hack that probably works really badly at best, and Tartareans aren't alive 

per se.

 So, debatable. But I think you mean 'ambulatory', which is just insane.

Chief Ibanez:

 Mad, even.

Dr. Okorie:

 Sure?

<Chief Ibanez nods, then heads down the path.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What prompted that?

Chief Ibanez:

 Just settling a bet. Nothing to worry about.

<Transcript ends.>

The following morning, Dr. Astrauskas scheduled a private meeting with Leandro Pelaez. He met her in the empty Ibanez shack.

<Transcript begins.>

<Dr. Astrauskas is seated in a battered steel chair. She has set up another for Leandro; he takes it, eyeing her suspiciously. She has no devices on her person, save for her lapel camera, and her hands are folded neatly in her lap.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Mr. Pelaez. We haven't been properly introduced. My name is Rozálie Astrauskas. I'm married to your daughter.

Leandro:

 I'm still waiting for someone to explain that to me.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 There will be plenty of time for that later.

<When he replies, his tone is petulant.>

Leandro:

 We have plenty of time right now. It's not like we can go anywhere.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I think you know that's not precisely true.

<He frowns.>

Leandro:

 Meaning?

<She leans forward, crossing her knees and placing both hands on them.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 How would you describe the problem with the mechanism in the Facility?

Leandro:

 Trying to catch me out?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Trying to see if we can all get on the same page. Indulge me?

Leandro:

 We ran out of flowers, and all the ones I tried to grow here are dead.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I believe the second part of that statement is true, if a little misleading.

Leandro:

 You're calling me a liar?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Yes.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Do you want to explain, or should I? Probably you'll want me to do it, in case we're not both thinking the same thing.

<Leandro shrugs.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Fine with me. The mechanism doesn't just need flowers, it needs flowers from the dimension you're trying to leave.

<Leandro's mouth twitches.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You don't really need to confirm. Dr. McDoctorate and I have it pretty well figured out.

Leandro:

 Dr. 

who?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 He'd be so pleased to hear you call him that.

<He waves dismissively at her, and turns to look out the open window. Chief Ibanez is using SCP-6500-SWORD to sharpen a farmer's plough in front of the blacksmith's shop, which has been converted out of the empty Lobo household shack. The blacksmith is watching, bemused. Saray is also watching; she is jumping up and down and swinging a stick while speaking with great excitement. Chief Ibanez is nodding indulgently.>

<Leandro scowls.>

Leandro:

 I don't know what you're talking about. All of this is nonsense.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You were the one responsible for replanting Stranger-in-the-Mist, right?

Leandro:

 Yes. That's one of my duties. The most important one.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 How come you were suddenly so bad at it?

<His head snaps back in her direction, and his tone becomes defensive.>

Leandro:

 There was nothing sudden about it. The old crop was dead, and the knowledge of how to grow a new one was never properly passed down to me.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 That's a good explanation. But the fact you've been dishonest with me about part of this process suggests—

<Leandro stands, and towers over her.>

Leandro:

 Suggests what? Why don't you just come out and say it?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Okay.

<She looks up at him, unflinching.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You killed your own crop.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 They grew just fine, so you killed them yourself.

Leandro:

 Why would I do that?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Because you saw the Facility vanish when Del called it back home, and you knew what that meant, and you didn't want to leave.

<He walks past her, into the back room. His voice carries easily in the steel shack.>

Leandro:

 Of course I want to leave. I've wanted to leave since the moment we got here.

<Dr. Astrauskas does not turn to watch him, but continues facing forward and speaking in an even tone.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Fine, you do 

want

 to leave. But you wouldn't let yourself do it. You were too afraid. So you stranded everyone here.

Leandro:

 What are you basing that on?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You never let Del or her sister or her brothers leave the village. I imagine the shield was a part of that, no? Made her dizzy when she climbed too high.

Leandro:

 They don't still have vertigo back on Earth?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 All your precautions, and still you couldn't protect them. So the second time around, you found a way to control the remaining variables.

Leandro:

 That's…

<Leandro has walked back into the main room. Across from Dr. Astrauskas, the front door is now open. Ursula is standing in the doorway.>

Leandro:

 Ursula.

Ursula:

 Leandro.

Leandro:

 You heard?

Ursula:

 I heard.

Leandro:

 Do you believe this?

Ursula:

 Of course I believe it. I've known the entire time.

<Silence on recording.>

<Leandro sags.>

Leandro:

 Do we need to tell them?

<Ursula walks into the shack, and attempts to comfort her husband.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It's true, then?

<Leandro spits on the floor, then looks mortified at having done so. He scuffs it out with his boot heel.>

Leandro:

 Of course it's true. This place might not look like much to you, but to me it's the only safe home I've ever had. Killing those flowers was the easiest thing I've ever had to do.

<Ursula embraces him.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Was it easy killing any chance of ever seeing me again? Killing the hope in your heart?

<She is standing at the window, which is partially ajar. Due to the buildup of soil and plant matter outside the shack, she is able to meet her father's eyes without craning her neck.>

Leandro:

 I thought you were dead.

Chief Ibanez:

 No, you didn't.

<She glances back over her shoulder, ensuring that Saray is still chatting with the blacksmith, who is inspecting the sharpened plow with an expression of astonishment. She then leans on the sill, and continues to speak.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I'm an investigator. No reason you should have known that. It's not like we've really talked yet. But the first day in this village, after speaking with your daughters, I went looking for something. Found it in your old laundry.

<Chief Ibanez unslings her backpack and unzips it. She removes a faded salmon dress, and drapes it over the windowsill before placing the bag on the ground beside her.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I left this here on the last day. I went for a swim in that bay—

<She points.>

Chief Ibanez:

 —and when I came back out, I started putting on the armour. Fired up the mechanism, and went back home to Zevala. Left the last thing that connected me to you, here.

<She stamps her foot for emphasis.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Did you find it, or someone else?

Leandro:

 I found it.

<Leandro is whispering now.>

Leandro:

 I was the first one out. I'm always the first one out.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Another of your duties.

Leandro:

 If something's going to happen to one of us, it should happen to me.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Why?

<He looks up, and straightens somewhat. Ursula withdraws.>

Leandro:

 Because you're right. It's always my fault. I wouldn't let them put the plan in motion. I wouldn't let them reach out for help. And I poured gasoline all over the flower crop.

Ursula:

 Leo…

Leandro:

 I'm sorry, Ursula.

Chief Ibanez:

 "The ashes of our last hope," you said.

Leandro:

 You knew.

Chief Ibanez:

 I've beaten the truth out of folks with a literally magical way with words. You're nothing by comparison.

<Ursula winces, but takes Leandro's hand.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I don't understand. You had the flowers, and you had the dress. You had to know there was a chance she was still alive out there.

Chief Ibanez:

 What are you talking about? Those flowers take ages to grow. Didn't he tell you the old ones had all died?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 He did tell me that.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Mr. Pelaez?

<He is shaking his head. He can't seem to stop.>

Leandro:

 I never took any chances, and even so, my children… my 

children…

<He raises his hands in a pleading gesture.>

Leandro:

 How could you expect me to go back?

Chief Ibanez:

 What's going on? The old flowers 

were

 already dead, right?

<Silence on recording.>

<Chief Ibanez is ashen.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Oh, my god.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You burned them too. In 1994, when you first arrived.

<Wordlessly, he nods. Once.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 How could you abandon your children?

Ursula:

 Because I forced him to.

<Chief Ibanez stares at her.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

Leandro:

 Ursula, no—

Ursula:

 When we first arrived, I went with him. It was against the rules, but after what we saw… the rules didn't seem to matter so much anymore.

<Leandro clutches her hand tightly.>

Ursula:

 I picked a flower, I ground it up, and while he was tending to the rest of the crop, I had a vision.

Chief Ibanez:

 A vision of what? Of what would happen if you tried to come back for me?

Ursula:

 Of whether or not we 

would

 try.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 And what did you see?

<She makes eye contact. Both women hold it for a time.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Obviously that you wouldn't.

Ursula:

 That's right.

Chief Ibanez:

 So you set that in stone. You made it so you could never come home, not without damaging reality further.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You were making it easier for him.

Chief Ibanez:

 Letting him let me go.

Leandro:

 I'm so sorry, Fina.

<He pulls himself together yet again.>

Leandro:

 But you're all safe here now. Long after everything else is perished, we'll still be here.

<Chief Ibanez picks up the sack again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Nothing else is going to perish. We're going to make sure of that, soon as we get back.

Leandro:

 Your friend is right.

Chief Ibanez:

 Wife.

Leandro:

 Your 

wife

 is right. The flowers need to be from here, and they don't grow anymore. I used the last of the seeds, and the plants are all dead. It would take decades to replace them.

Chief Ibanez:

 Pack some supplies, and meet me at the gulch tomorrow morning.

Leandro:

 Why?

Chief Ibanez:

 You're going to show me.

Leandro:

 But…

<He sighs in desperate frustration.>

Leandro:

 They're dead, I told you.

Chief Ibanez:

 Never stopped me before.

<Transcript ends.>

As requested, before heading back out Chief Ibanez engaged in a brief consultation with Dr. McDoctorate. The latter was adamant that no record of their conversation be made.

Chief Ibanez and Leandro Pelaez left Puerto Extirpado again the following day, at first light. They travelled together to the altered treeline, at which point Chief Ibanez again left her escort on the shore before walking into the bog, SCP-6500-SWORD in hand.

The pair returned to the village at sunset.

<Transcript begins.>

<Dr. Okorie exits the Ibanez shack, stretching her back and grunting. It is late evening, and the invisible sun is setting; Puerto Extirpado is bathed in a fierce greenish-yellow glow, and verdant spores begin to catch the light all around her. They are much thicker than usual, settling over the rolling plateau like a blanket. She yawns, and takes a single step in the direction of the gully when a small stone skitters across her path, followed by a filthy brown boot, followed by its owner.>

<Chief Ibanez appears around the corner of the shack. Her jumpsuit hangs at her waist, and her armour is deeply scored and plastered with dried green mud. The entire right sleeve, most of the left, and both cuffs are missing. Her hair is alternately slick and matted with more mud which gleams dully in the dying light, or dripping with rotted mulch; even more mud covers every exposed inch of her body and attire, and she leaves a trail of it on the grass behind her. Two bands of rebar encircle her exposed abdomen, presumably bearing the weight of SCP-6500-SWORD which hangs behind her, glowing warmly, sheathe and harness apparently discarded. It is difficult to tell beneath the grime, but she appears physically unharmed.>

<Slowly, theatrically, she flexes the muscles of her right arm.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What the fuck happened?

<Chief Ibanez jerks a thumb at herself.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What did you happen to?

<Chief Ibanez grins.>

Chief Ibanez returns.

Chief Ibanez:

 Wholeass dragon.

<She claws hair out of her face, and wipes the sweat from her brow.>

Chief Ibanez:

 This time it 

took.

Dr. Okorie:

 Fina, Warrior Princess.

<Both laugh.>

<Dr. Astrauskas exits the shack, turns, and freezes when she sees Chief Ibanez.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 What the hell happened?

<Chief Ibanez and Dr. Okorie laugh again.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Where's your father?

Chief Ibanez:

 Dragging the sack.

Dr. Okorie:

 What sack?

<Transcript ends.>

Leandro Pelaez arrived at Facility-34 half an hour later with Chief Ibanez's bag in tow, filled to the brim with 

N. cerritulus

 revitalized via the anomalous properties of a hyper-energized SCP-6500-SWORD. Dr. McDoctorate performed his baseline tests a second time, and indicated that the TLP's 'pilot light' was now back on. It was possible to return to baseline reality.

The villagers of Puerto Extirpado were informed that a transference would take place the following day, and they should prepare their structures and remove all vital personal possessions to the Facility. A feast was held in the town square using the remainder of their perishable goods, after which Delta-6500 met with the Ibanez/Pelaez family for a final debriefing.

<Transcript begins.>

<It is late. Chief Ibanez and Leandro have showered and changed into fresh clothing, and the adults are drinking homemade malt beer from malformed green glass bottles around the kitchen table, except for Pilar who is lying on the floor, sound asleep and snoring.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 All's well that ends well.

Ursula:

 Have you ever heard of tempting fate, Dr. Place?

<He laughs.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Don't get me started.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 He means that. Don't.

Dr. Okorie:

 You look pretty gutted, Mr. Pelaez.

Leandro:

 Just call me Leandro, please.

Dr. Okorie:

 Leandro. I know you've got misgivings—

<A tear rolls down his cheek. He doesn't bother to brush it away.>

Leandro:

 It's not even that.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Then what?

Leandro:

 I just saw my daughter do something I never thought possible. It still seems impossible. It was already impossible to even see her again.

<Dr. Okorie reaches out to hold his hand. He is surprised, but allows the contact.>

Dr. Okorie:

 She does that a lot. You won't get used to it, but you will get used to expecting it.

<He shakes his head.>

Leandro:

 I never imagined anything like that could be under the ground. I didn't even believe Saray when she told me about her birds.

Dr. Okorie:

 They might not have existed until recently.

<He frowns.>

Leandro:

 How's that?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 This world is waking up.

Leandro:

 What does that mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 Nothing good for ours.

<He appears to give up attempting to understand, and sighs deeply.>

Leandro:

 I never wanted any of this for you, Fina.

<She shrugs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It's not your problem anymore. It's mine. So you can either help me fix it, or stay out of my way.

<He nods.>

Leandro:

 I don't know what help I can be, but you…

<He smiles tentatively.>

Leandro:

 You are a 

wonder.

 Now and always. You only need to ask.

<Dr. Astrauskas tugs at Chief Ibanez's cheek. The latter scowls, but does not resist.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Our miracle worker.

<Leandro swirls his bottle, staring at the liquid through the distortion of the glass, then takes a deep breath as though he is building up his courage.>

Leandro:

 How did the three of you meet?

Dr. Okorie:

 Roz was in my cohort as a novice thaumaturge. Del was Chief of Security where we worked.

Chief Ibanez:

 Then lots of people died, and here we are.

<Leandro blinks.>

Ursula:

 Our people have married outside the village often, of course. And our ancestors did the same.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Can't sustain a population that low without exogamy. Not healthily, at least.

Ursula:

 My point is, you're not the only one to leave home to find love.

Chief Ibanez:

 I never left home. Home left me.

<She empties her bottle, and claps it to the table with finality.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Leandro. You offered, now I'm asking. No more secrets.

Ursula:

 I think that's for the best.

Chief Ibanez:

 What was the Chaos Insurgency doing in Zevala?

<Leandro stands, and leaves the room for a moment to check on where Saray is sleeping. When he returns, he shuts the door behind him before sitting down again and looking under the table at Pilar. She is still snoring.>

Leandro:

 They were building something.

Chief Ibanez:

 I know that. What were they building?

Ursula:

 We never heard. We never even asked. They shot anyone who said anything they didn't like.

Leandro:

 Your mother…

<Chief Ibanez raises a hand, a look of warning in her eyes.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I know more about that than you do. But come on. You were all cooped up in their cages for weeks. You must have learned something.

Leandro:

 Why is that important? It was so long ago.

Chief Ibanez:

 Because the Insurgency is toast, but the kind of shit they were into? It lingers. We don't understand why they were so focused on Zevala, and we don't know how they're connected to the rest of what's going on, and we can't very well ask them.

Leandro:

 Didn't you take any prisoners?

Chief Ibanez:

 Me?

<She scoffs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 No.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 And trust me, they had an even bigger taste for cyanide than they had for blue flowers.

<Silence on recording.>

Ursula:

 I really do not know, Delfina.

Leandro:

 I do.

Ursula:

 What?

Leandro:

 They kept me separate from the others. Made me do things. Tell them things.

<He shakes his head at the implied question in his wife's eyes.>

Leandro:

 I'm not going to expand on that. It wouldn't do anybody any good to know. What matters is we're all still alive because of it.

Chief Ibanez:

 Not all of us. Those people you sold us out to—

Leandro:

 I didn't sell anyone out.

Chief Ibanez:

 Then who did? How did they find us, d—…?

<She picks up the bottle again, and swills the last few drops. He waits a moment for her to finish, and resume speaking; when she does not, he does.>

Leandro:

 Mostly what they wanted was information. A lot of it was about the Facility.

Chief Ibanez:

 Like what?

Leandro:

 What it did. How it worked. I played dumb, gave them little tidbits here and there like I was only just now putting the pieces together. Stalling until I saw my chance to get away. To get everyone away.

Chief Ibanez:

 And you heard things?

Leandro:

 Heard, and saw. They were building something in one of the crevasses. Something big and shiny. And it was taking something out of the air.

Chief Ibanez:

 Taking what?

Leandro:

 I don't know. They called it a Hume collector. It was on for weeks, and it chugged through an ungodly amount of fuel. Smoked like a bastard. I think it was draining all the life out of the bay. You remember the sunsets?

<Chief Ibanez nods.>

Leandro:

 They were never the same after that thing was turned on.

Ursula:

 And the flowers.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Stranger-in-the-Mist?

Ursula:

 They dredged up the entire cargo from the 

Northern Reach.

 I know that much.

Leandro:

 And they fed it all in.

<Dr. McDoctorate suddenly drums the table in triumph. Beneath, Pilar stirs but does not wake.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I knew it! I 

knew

 it.

<Dr. Astrauskas leans over, and they share a high-five.>

Leandro:

 What did you know?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I don't have all the right equipment for this — it was only just invented, after all, which is why nobody ever ran the tests before — but I was able to jury-rig some of what I found in the Facility, and it gave us a very strong—

Chief Ibanez:

 Tonight, Place.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 We know why the 

Nigella

 in the hydroponics worked for all universes, probably.

Leandro:

 I never figured that out myself. The man who taught me didn't know.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It was Dr. Astrauskas who cracked it, really.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It was half my magic and half your science. You're much too modest.

Chief Ibanez:

 He really isn't.

Dr. Okorie:

 What did you guys figure out, though?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 That these flowers grow in every dimension. They 

exist

 in every dimension. And I don't just mean versions of them. The same flowers. The same 

instances

 of the same flowers. They're entangled across the timeplane. They're a multiversal constant. The name is a misnomer; these flowers are strange to 

nowhere.

<The others exchange glances.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Then again, maybe 

that's

 what it means. Strange to nowhere. Strangers 

only

 in the mist, the inter-universal gulf where nothing grows but nothing.

<He shakes himself out of his musing.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 But that's why they give visions. They're connected to every reality.

Chief Ibanez:

 The same flowers blooming under every sun.

Ursula:

 That's beautiful.

Leandro:

 And I let you wear them in your hair.

Ursula:

 That's beautiful, too.

<He looks away. There are tears in his eyes.>

Dr. Okorie:

 But what does that have to do with the hydroponics?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 

Nigella

 grown in the Facility aren't in any universe. It's a pocket all its own. They're Hume-neutral, and can access the entire set without corrupting the data with local identifiers. That's why they let the TLP get a fix on so many coordinates, and you just have to pick one and see where it goes.

Dr. Okorie:

 Maybe that's what the time dilation was for, too. Maybe it was intentional.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Hmm?

Dr. Okorie:

 So the Facility could regrow its crop without taking up thirty years real-time.

<His eyes widen.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I really do love how smart we all are. You know that?

Leandro:

 I don't think I will ever understand how people like you exist.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Thank you!

<Dr. Okorie nudges Dr. McDoctorate.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What was your secret little chat with Del about? Before she went out to kill the dragon?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Isn't it obvious? He told her to kill the dragon so the sword could power up and bring the plants back to life.

Chief Ibanez:

 That was my idea. He said it wouldn't work.

Dr. Okorie:

 But… it 

did

 work.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Powering up the sword was only half of it. Leandro wasn't lying when he said the plants didn't grow well here. That's because their leyline wasn't reliable.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 There 

is

 no leyline. We established that.

Dr. Okorie:

 But then they could never have grown at all. Wait a fucking second.

<Chief Ibanez snorts.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Do you get it?

Dr. Okorie:

 No way.

Chief Ibanez:

 

Do you get it?

Leandro:

 What?

Dr. Okorie:

 Ambulatory leylines.

Leandro:

 What?

Dr. Okorie:

 The dragon?

Chief Ibanez:

 The dragon.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I do wish I could have seen it.

<Leandro grimaces.>

Leandro:

 You can have my memories.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Not in my skillset. That's Udo's territory.

Leandro:

 Huh?

Dr. Okorie:

 It's a shame none of the camera footage is clear.

 I'll make sure to bring a Steadicam next time.

<She places a sketch on the table.>

Extranormal Entity, rendering by SCP-8273-2.

 Oh. 

Wow.

 You fought 

that?

 Pilar drew this? It's beautiful.

Ursula:

 You should see the wood carvings Saray has been working on.

<Silence on recording.>

Ursula:

 You really should have just come back home, you silly man.

<Leandro flushes, and turns to Chief Ibanez.>

Leandro:

 What artistic talents have you picked up? Since this is apparently a family of prodigies.

Chief Ibanez:

 Harpsichord. I got into the Royal Academy, but had to defer for a semester so I could see the worlds.

Ursula:

 If I might interrupt. Your plan was to kill the dragon, Delfina. His plan was 

also

 to kill the dragon. Why did he say your plan wouldn't work?

 Her plan was to kill it for the wrong reason. Intentionality matters—

Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie:

 [simultaneously] —when it comes to magic.

 This is 

insanity.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why did you think I lured it to the plantation before killing it?

<Leandro purses his lips.>

Leandro:

 Honestly?

<She nods.>

Leandro:

 I thought you wanted to frighten me.

<All laugh.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It does mean we really do have to be moving on, though.

 Why?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Because that thing was more than just a living leyline. I got the data from the atmospheric collectors we set up around the ridge, and compared it to the dragon guts on Delfina's ruined clothing, and—

Chief Ibanez:

 You went through my laundry?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Woman, I was 

doing

 your laundry.

<All laugh.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 The dragon was algal. It was a spore-creature. The same spores we see in the sky every morning and every night.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 By the same, you mean—

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I mean the air we breath is dragon's breath. Yes.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Okorie:

 I 

thought

 they were getting pretty thick, these last couple days.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 You slew this world's primordial deity, Chief. Or one of them. No matter what else happens next, nothing will be the same. Your coming marked the end of this world's mythical age. The advent of heroes.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Mother of the future.

Dr. Okorie:

 Prometheus with a sword.

<Chief Ibanez looks up at the ceiling, reflectively.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 I didn't mean to harsh your buzz with an inconvenient truth.

<She shoots him a dirty look.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I can't think of anything to say about that.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Segue!

Chief Ibanez:

 Segue! What were we… right. The machine. The other one. The one the Insurgency was making. What did it 

do?

Leandro:

 Calculations, I heard. Lots and lots of calculations.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Calculations they could only do in Zevala.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Or with something unique to its environment.

Dr. Okorie:

 Particles in the air. The stuff I was detecting.

 The festivals.

 What?

 What were the festivals? What were they really?

<Ursula and Leandro exchange a glance.>

Ursula:

 We took the village…

 Elsewhere.

 I saw the sky change.

 Of course you did.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why? Why do that?

Ursula:

 It's what we've always done. The Prophets started it.

Leandro:

 It helped protect us. Replenished our defences. Put something in the air that fed the machine that strengthened the dome.

Chief Ibanez:

 You'd stopped doing it by the time I was a teenager.

Leandro:

 The machine was too far gone by then, and we didn't know how to repair it.

Ursula:

 That's not entirely true. We didn't exactly lose sleep over the decision. We already thought it was too dangerous.

Leandro:

 We thought the defences were strong enough already.

Ursula:

 We thought it would bring unwanted attention.

Chief Ibanez:

 The Insurgency?

Leandro:

 The Foundation.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 But that's what let them in, isn't it?

Leandro:

 Maybe. Probably. If you ask me, Dom Magnusson sold us out.

Dr. Okorie:

 Who?

Chief Ibanez:

 Captain of the 

Northern Reach.

 If he was in on it, he sure got paid for his trouble.

 Is this why the dome hardened before it fell? Why nothing could go in or out? Was that a symptom of it failing, because you didn't keep it fuelled up?

Dr. McDoctorate:

 That's one possibility. It might also have been reacting to the firefight in the sky, closing up shop to protect everyone.

 Worked great, didn't it.

Ursula:

 What does it matter? What does one more thing that went wrong matter in the long litany? Can't you just let these things go?

Leandro:

 She's right to question us. We kept so much from them all.

Chief Ibanez:

 All I care about is seeing this thing through. If the Insurgency was building a machine that ran on the emissions of the Facility, or the air in the alternate dimensions…

<Her eyes suddenly widen, and her mouth snaps shut.>

Dr. Okorie:

 No.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Alternate dimensions.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Multiversal data sets.

Dr. Okorie:

 The flowers.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 The aura variations.

Chief Ibanez:

 Fuel. 

Churning.

Dr. Okorie:

 Calculations.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Probability.

Dr. Okorie:

 

No.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Are we saying…

Dr. McDoctorate:

 It's the only logical explanation. And the timeline works.

<Drs. Astrauskas, McDoctorate and Okorie each look as though they wish to speak next, but something is holding them back.>

<Chief Ibanez makes eye contact with all three in turn, then finally nods.>

Chief Ibanez:

 That's it, then.

<They nod back, one by one.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It's the Engine. They were building the Engine.

<Leandro and Ursula are looking back and forth between the four of them.

Leandro:

 What Engine?

 Never mind. I understand now. It let them triangulate. Build up a sort of… cosmic cheat sheet. Visions of the future. Visions they could act on. Oh, Jesus.

Dr. Okorie:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 This changed everything. This 

changed

 everything.

<Drs. Astrauskas, McDoctorate and Okorie are in obvious shock. None speak until Chief Ibanez prompts them again.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Zevala is the reason the Insurgency couped itself.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 Reorganized around the Engine.

Dr. Okorie:

 Change.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 

Change.

Chief Ibanez:

 

Delta

 Command.

<Dr. Okorie whistles.>

Leandro:

 What does all this mean?

Chief Ibanez:

 It means you gave the worst people in the world a road map to conquest.

Ursula:

 Conquest of what?

Chief Ibanez:

 Everything.

Leandro:

 But you said they were destroyed.

Dr. McDoctorate:

 The Engine predicted the future for them, but its predictions stopped being correct a couple years back. Very badly. Something else intervened, and changed the nature of causality. We're still trying to determine what.

Chief Ibanez:

 But that doesn't matter, not in this context. The Insurgency were only the hand of something bigger. Only 

one

 hand. And they rowed us a long, long way down the river before we cut that hand off.

Ursula:

 Is there anything we can do to fix it?

Chief Ibanez:

 There's one thing.

<She stands, walks to the icebox, and begins retrieving a new set of green bottles.>

Chief Ibanez:

 It's time we brought those sunsets back to Argentina.

<The scientists and Chief Ibanez are spending the night in the shack, room having been made by the removal of most of the family's possessions to Facility-34. As they lie on their bedrolls, still inebriated, Chief Ibanez turns to face Dr. Astrauskas.>

Chief Ibanez:

 How did you make sense of it?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Hmm?

Chief Ibanez:

 The thing with the flowers?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Oh.

<Dr. Astrauskas yawns.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 You're not the only one who learned a new thing in that Facility. I tried something I've never tried before.

Chief Ibanez:

 Don't keep me in suspense. I'll snap before I bend.

<Silence on recording.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Engineering joke.

Chief Ibanez:

 Engineering joke.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I read the aura of the flowers we brought with us.

Chief Ibanez:

 Flowers have auras?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Most living things do, but not as complex when they aren't sapient. It only occurred to me to look when I saw the Leading Edge had one. I just wondered. And what I saw was the most incredible little constellation of interlocking Hume spirals you can imagine.

Chief Ibanez:

 I can't imagine that at all.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I'll draw you a pretty diagram when we get back. Suffice to say I had to go on antipsychotics after. It was… a strain.

<Chief Ibanez reaches out and interlocks their fingers. A tear rolls down Dr. Astrauskas' cheek.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 They find each other. The flowers. Across all that empty. They stay connected. Entangled. It's…

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah.

<Dr. Astrauskas clears her throat.>

Dr. Astrauskas:

 So after I saw that, I went back down to hydroponics, and checked out all those dead twigs. Hume spirals leave a residuum which lasts a good long while after death, but it should have run out by now. Luckily, time in here is all screwy, so.

Chief Ibanez:

 Declension and elevation. You could see they'd been using flowers from other dimensions, and storing them alive in the hydroponics.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 I could. It was only a few out of thousands, probably just as an insurance policy. But I knew.

Chief Ibanez:

 Still a bit of a logical leap, wasn't it? I mean, presumably they were growing plants across the multiverse for practical purposes too. Not wanting to rely on the Facility's freezer. That didn't necessarily mean it was a requirement.

Dr. Astrauskas:

 No, you're right. I did make an educated guess.

Chief Ibanez:

 Based on what?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Your father seemed so guilty. I knew he couldn't be telling the truth. The way he told it, it wasn't his fault.

<Chief Ibanez embraces her where they lie.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Roz, there's a lot you don't know about how guilt works, and I hope you never do.

<Dr. Okorie embraces her from behind.>

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Flora aura.

Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie:

 [simultaneously] Shut up.

<Laughter.>

<Transcript ends.>

The following morning, the sun visibly rose over Puerto Extirpado for the first time. The haze had shifted from the horizon to the hills around the village, spores wafting in on the breeze.

After a brief vigil to observe this phenomenon, the villagers were evacuated to Facility-34. Dr. McDoctorate and his technicians prepared to return the Facility to baseline reality, with Leandro providing the requisite data to include the village's standing structures in the transference. Two hours before the scheduled transit, Ursula asked a favour of Chief Ibanez.

<Transcript begins.>

<The residents of Puerto Extirpado are milling about in the foyer and halls, the majority of their belongings in Institute-issue backpacks and bags carried on their persons. They are not unpacking, as the transit is expected to be over within the hour.>

<Chief Ibanez is watching Saray. The latter is holding the pommel of a sheathed SCP-6500-SWORD, and reciting a litany of her own accomplishments in the alternate dimension. Occasionally, a brief flicker can be seen from the exposed few centimetres of blade. She crows in delight each time this occurs.>

<Ursula approaches Chief Ibanez.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Everybody settled?

Ursula:

 Unsettled. But that's the idea, right?

Chief Ibanez:

 Yeah. Where's Pilar?

Ursula:

 And your father?

<Chief Ibanez shrugs.>

Ursula:

 Speaking with your wives.

<Chief Ibanez grimaces.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Any chance you could break that up?

Ursula:

 I propose a trade of favours.

Chief Ibanez:

 Saving your asses isn't enough?

Ursula:

 You're doing that as much for yourself as for us, I think.

<Silence on recording.>

Ursula:

 There is something I would like to try.

Chief Ibanez:

 Shoot.

Saray:

 Bang!

<The adults look down at her. She grins sheepishly.>

Ursula:

 I have never had a vision between worlds.

<Chief Ibanez looks back up at her.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I've never had strawberry shortcake.

Ursula:

 It's very good. I could make you some, if you like. Just need the strawberries.

Saray:

 What's a strawberry?

Chief Ibanez:

 What would be different about having a vision mid-transit?

Ursula:

 On the other side, the visions are locked to the future of that world. I wonder if maybe…

Chief Ibanez:

 You can get something of more cosmic significance in between.

Ursula:

 That's right.

Chief Ibanez:

 You don't need to be somewhere to be somewhere.

Ursula:

 What?

Chief Ibanez:

 Nothing. What makes you so confident these visions are accurate? Nothing I've seen is falsifiable. It's all either vague stuff, or stuff we don't yet understand.

Ursula:

 We have seen one thing which came to pass precisely as foretold.

Chief Ibanez:

 Which is what?

<Ursula looks down at Saray again.>

<Chief Ibanez puts her hand on the little girl's shoulders, and steers her away.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Go play in traffic.

Saray:

 What's traffic?

<Chief Ibanez points at Dr. McDoctorate, who is attempting to pass through the throng without being drawn into conversation.>

Chief Ibanez:

 That's traffic. Go get him.

<Saray bounds off toward Dr. McDoctorate, who attempts to force a smile as he notices her approaching.>

Chief Ibanez:

 One vision came true.

Ursula:

 Yes.

Chief Ibanez:

 What did you see?

Ursula:

 The destruction of Zevala.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 No.

Ursula:

 Yes.

<Chief Ibanez sits down on the bench, next to SCP-6500-SWORD, then immediately stands up again and begins pacing.>

Chief Ibanez:

 

No.

 Don't tell me you knew that was going to happen.

Ursula:

 We did.

Chief Ibanez:

 Who's 'we'?

Ursula:

 Your mother and I.

<Chief Ibanez stops in her tracks.>

Chief Ibanez:

 She… you…?

Ursula:

 She was one of the seers, yes. We saw it together.

Chief Ibanez:

 You knew the Insurgency was going to come.

Ursula:

 Yes.

Chief Ibanez:

 Did you know when?

Ursula:

 No.

Chief Ibanez:

 But you still could have stopped it.

Ursula:

 Possibly.

Chief Ibanez:

 And you didn't even try.

Ursula:

 That's right. That was the last vision she ever had.

Chief Ibanez:

 When?

Ursula:

 About a year before you were born.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 She knew she was going to die?

Ursula:

 We didn't see the details. Just the fire in the sky, reflected on the bay. But we understood the meaning.

Chief Ibanez:

 How could you let it happen?

Ursula:

 Because we knew we couldn't fail our responsibility to the future twice. We understood the rules too well. Reality would unravel.

<Ursula wipes at her eyes.>

Chief Ibanez:

 So, the attack was your penance. Paid by everyone I ever knew.

<She glances at SCP-6500-SWORD, as though considering drawing it from its sheathe.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Did my mother…

Ursula:

 She wanted to flee. She thought about taking you all and running, maybe securing passage with one of the smuggler ships.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why didn't she?

Ursula:

 We had the vision together, but we didn't see precisely the same things. She said… she knew you needed to stay. You needed to be there for it.

Chief Ibanez:

 Why? Why was it so important we be there when the sky fell?

<Ursula shakes her head.>

Ursula:

 Not all of you. Not your sister, or your brothers. Only you. And…

Chief Ibanez:

 What?

Ursula:

 If she defied the visions, where could she flee to? And what would she be leaving behind? She told me… she told me she couldn't destroy your world. It came down to that, in the end.

Chief Ibanez:

 My world was destroyed anyway.

Ursula:

 Not all of it.

<Chief Ibanez clenches her jaw.>

Chief Ibanez:

 If this is your attempt to convince me there's something to this bullshit, you took completely the wrong tack.

Ursula:

 Trust your mother, Fina.

Chief Ibanez:

 Fina is dead, and so is my mother.

Ursula:

 She believed so strongly in you, she was willing to die just to give you a chance. A fighting chance. Do this for her. Let 

me

 do this for her.

<Chief Ibanez sighs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I just don't see why we need to give ourselves an obligation to the future. Feels like an unforced error.

Ursula:

 Delfina, our biggest mistake was forgetting that we 

always

 have an obligation to the future.

<Silence on recording.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Fine. I'll ask Place if he can suss out how the handbrake works. But try to make it a nice vision, alright? I can't even keep all these god damn revelations straight in my head as it is.

<Ursula places a hand on her shoulder.>

Ursula:

 Tomorrow is a promise, but I'm afraid I can't make any.

<Chief Ibanez pulls out her data pad, and scans a schematic of the Facility.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Guess we'll have to settle for making the future itself.

Ursula:

 You've been talking to Pilar.

Chief Ibanez:

 Listening. There's a difference.

<Ursula is sitting on a couch in one of the Facility-34 dormitories. The fabric is an unfamiliar polymer, and has not degraded through years of disuse; the Facility air recyclers have deposited a great deal of dust everywhere, but Ursula has made the room habitable with her novel discovery of a vacuum cleaner.>

<Chief Ibanez is sitting in a wooden dining chair, watching as the older woman crushes a single specimen of

 N. cerritulus 

with a stone mortar and pestle.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Place says running the stabilization cycle should be enough. We don't need to pull an actual transit for your vision. We should be partially de-realized now, and it'll last about twenty minutes.

 That's good. I'd like to be there with the others to witness when we finally leave home for good.

<The door to the room opens, and Chief Ibanez turns to see Pilar.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I didn't tell anyone where we went.

Pilar:

 You didn't have to. You're the local celebrity. Everyone knows where you are.

<She sits down on the couch beside her mother.>

Ursula:

 I want to share the vision.

Pilar:

 Well?

 She doesn't. I mean in general.

<Ursula sighs.>

Ursula:

 You're an adult, and it 

is

 your birthright. And we might learn something interesting if we try.

 How's that?

Ursula:

 She's not from Earth at all. She was born in Puerto Extirpado. It's possible she'll bring something even more foreign to the vision.

Chief Ibanez:

 It's 

not

<Pilar smiles warmly at her.>

Ursula:

Pilar:

 Draw your finger through the bowl, then place the mixture on your tongue. That's all.

Pilar:

 No mystical chants?

Chief Ibanez:

Pilar:

 What's Argentina?

<Silence on recording.>

<Chief Ibanez and Ursula laugh.>

Pilar:

 What?

Pilar:

<Chief Ibanez raises an eyebrow.>

Ursula:

 Are you ready?

<Pilar straightens her back on the couch, and nods.>

<Ursula reaches around her daughter's shoulders and presses her down until she relaxes again, then holds the mortar out to her.>

<Both women draw a portion of the mixture from the bowl, and press it to their tongues. They sit back on the couch, and share a look.>

<Chief Ibanez looks back and forth between the two of them.>

Chief Ibanez:

 When does it start?

<Mother and daughter are still staring at each other, intently. Their eyes begin moving rapidly.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Oh.

Ursula:

 I see infinity.

Chief Ibanez:

 That's a lot.

<Neither woman gives any physiological sign that she can hear Chief Ibanez.>

Ursula:

 All is colour and brilliance. I can see farther than the farthest light. I can see each mote of dust. I am at the heart of all things.

<Pilar winces, but says nothing.>

Ursula:

 They are arguing.

Chief Ibanez:

 Who's arguing?

<Ursula squints. She looks afraid.>

Ursula:

 Oh, they are angry. They are both so 

very

 angry.

 I should have had Udo put her brain reader thing in your skulls.

<Still Pilar does not speak.>

Ursula:

 They are apart. They have been 

set

 apart.

<She smiles wickedly.>

Ursula:

 It worked. It really worked.

Chief Ibanez:

<Ursula suddenly starts. Her eyes roll back in her skull.>

Ursula:

 I don't understand.

<Chief Ibanez leans in, but does not ask another question.>

Ursula:

 I don't… I don't 

understand.

 Why are you doing that, Pilar?

<Pilar is twitching, and clenching the surface of the couch cushion she sits on.>

Ursula:

 No!

<Her eyes snap open.>

<She looks at Pilar.>

<Pilar is weeping.>

<Ursula draws her daughter into an embrace, and begins singing softly into her ear. Her voice is too quiet to be discerned.>

<Pilar awakens, and clutches desperately at her mother.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What did you see? Both of you?

<Ursula looks at her, clearly troubled.>

Ursula:

 Did you hear what I said?

Chief Ibanez:

 I heard.

Ursula:

 The stars were wheeling all around, and I was watching them fall. Not the stars, but 

them.

Chief Ibanez:

 The brothers.

<Ursula nods.>

Ursula:

<She cries out.>

Ursula:

we are going to make it so much worse.

Ursula:

Ursula:

 It doesn't mean 

anything.

 Okay. What did you see, Pilar?

Chief Ibanez:

 Good idea. She's too much like me.

<Ursula smiles sadly.>

Ursula:

 They both are.

<With a meaningful look at Pilar, she leaves the dormitory, closing the door behind her.>

<Pilar shudders.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You lie to her very often?

<Pilar stares at her, then bursts into laughter. It is high and almost manic.>

Chief Ibanez:

 What did you see?

Pilar:

 I didn't see any of what she saw.

<She takes a deep breath, and shudders.>

Pilar:

 I was standing on the shore of a lake. It was blue. I've never seen a blue lake before, or a blue sky. But sometimes the sky wasn't blue. Sometimes it was red, and sometimes black, and there was no lake at all, and the world was just this endless mass of boxes on boxes on boxes, and sometimes everything 

crawled,

 and… I saw all of you.

Chief Ibanez:

 All of who?

Pilar:

 You. Your people. I've never seen them before, but I knew who they were. There were so many of them, but it was never enough.

Chief Ibanez:

 It has to be enough.

Pilar:

 It won't be.

Chief Ibanez:

 I promise you—

Pilar:

 I saw you die.

<Chief Ibanez shrugs.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Okay.

<Pilar's eyes widen, and her brows knit.>

Pilar:

 Okay?! How is that okay?!

Chief Ibanez:

 I've never been afraid to die. The first time I realized I could, I didn't care. I haven't started caring since.

<Pilar examines her sister's face.>

Pilar:

 Is that true?

<She shakes her head. Her breathing is rapid and uneven. She appears to be near to a panic attack.>

<Chief Ibanez reaches out and takes her hand.>

Pilar:

 But it's not what I meant. Delfina.

Chief Ibanez:

 Then what did you mean?

Pilar:

 I mean 

I saw you die.

<Silence on recording.>

Pilar:

 All of you.

<Transcript ends.>

In final preparation for the transit, the Extirpadans engaged in their unsevering ritual in the foyer of Facility-34. There is no documentation or recording testifying to the nature of this ritual, as by their request no Foundation personnel were to attend the ceremony — save for Chief Ibanez.

She declined to offer testimony about what she saw and heard, though she did make a few brief observations in the presence of Dr. Okorie.

<Transcript begins.>

<Dr. Okorie is waiting in the hall when Chief Ibanez emerges, looking dazed. The Extirpadans are collecting their effects again, and speaking with each other in hushed tones.>

<Chief Ibanez spits a single blue seed into a trash bin by the door.>

Dr. Okorie:

 You okay?

<Chief Ibanez nods.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What's wrong?

Chief Ibanez:

 It's just…

<She staggers to the nearest bench, and sits down on it heavily.>

Dr. Okorie:

 Del?

Chief Ibanez:

 I already knew it, but know I… now I know it. I can feel it. For certain.

Dr. Okorie:

 What? What do you know?

Chief Ibanez:

 That's why it left me behind.

<Dr. Okorie waits for clarification.>

Chief Ibanez:

 I wasn't there for the ritual when they left me. I was still severed.

<Dr. Okorie sits down, and puts her arms around her.>

Dr. Okorie:

 But you stayed connected anyway.

<The two embrace.>

Dr. Okorie:

 And you've been making more connections ever since.

<Chief Ibanez sighs.>

Dr. Okorie:

 And showing me up, in the process.

<Chief Ibanez pulls back, and looks up at Dr. Okorie in confusion.>

Dr. Okorie:

 I meet one long-lost sister, you've got to one-up me and find two.

<Chief Ibanez laughs, then shoves Dr. Okorie back to her side of the bench.>

<Dr. Astrauskas rounds the corner, sees the two of them, and smiles broadly.>

Chief Ibanez:

 You want some too?

<Dr. Astrauskas continues to smile, and says nothing.>

Chief Ibanez:

 

What.

 Am I wearing something of yours?

Dr. Okorie:

 Roz?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 Remember what I said about your Hume spirals being broken?

<With the ritual complete, all personnel reported ready for the TLP's activation.>

<Chief Ibanez stands at the controls to the machine, Dr. McDoctorate beside her and Drs. Astrauskas and Okorie behind with Leandro and Ursula Pelaez, and their daughters. The Extirpadans are holding hands.>

Pilar:

 What about the bodies?

<Ursula frowns.>

Ursula:

 What?

Pilar:

 They're not alive, and they're… still biological. You know what I mean. The machine won't target them, will it? Are we leaving them behind? In the graveyard?

<Chief Ibanez glances back at them.>

<Leandro has difficulty speaking. His voice is hoarse.>

Leandro:

 We're not leaving them behind, big fish. They're coming with us.

<He raises her hand, and presses it against his heart.>

Leandro:

 Always with us.

<Pilar bites her upper lip.>

Dr. McDoctorate:

 All green.

Pilar:

 Story of my life.

<Chief Ibanez glances back at her, a glint in her eye.>

Ursula:

Leandro:

 No.

<The entire group turns to look at him.>

Leandro:

 This is the last trip.

<He makes eye contact with Chief Ibanez as Pilar and Ursula hold his hands tighter.>

<She nods.>

<She turns back to the console.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Let's go home.

<She presses the button.>

<As before, the TLP spins to life, and reality collapses like a television signal before abruptly reasserting itself. The process takes no more than one minute, though time is severely dilated.>

<The light subsides, and the machine spins back down. The group exchange glances.>

Chief Ibanez:

 Welcome back to b—

<There is an earsplitting CRACK, and the floor shakes.>

<Chief Ibanez reaches for her radio as it crackles to life. The voice of Captain Seon Ji-Hun fills the air.>

Captain Seon:

 Delta-6500, that had better be you.

<There is a second CRACK, now obviously representing a distant explosion. The next is not so distant; the lights flicker, and one of the ceiling tiles falls. Pilar screams.>

Dr. Okorie:

 What the hell is—

 This is Delta-6500 actual! Report!

 Aerial assault. Bombers with fighter escort. Lost contact with sentries in the forest, might be ground pounders on their way too. No positive ID yet.

Chief Ibanez:

 Who else could it be?

Dr. Astrauskas:

 It can't be. Not anymore.

Chief Ibanez:

 What planet have you been living on? There's no not anymore anymore. This is just the way shit is now.

Chief Ibanez:

 Hold the line, cap. We'll back you up.

 Never any doubts, Chief.

 You hearing this, Nasty?

Agent Koslova:

 Loud and.

 You and Georgiy get to the Zevala-side airlock. You're gonna have civilians to protect.

 Roger roger.

Chief Ibanez:

 Roz, you watch the villagers. Use your juju to identify anybody who looks like they're gonna try and be a hero.

 Right.

 Caves collapse.

 Fuck no. I learned my lesson. This time the Warrior and the Warlock take one path, together.

<She grabs Dr. Okorie's hand, and pulls her out of the control room in the direction of the armoury.>

Chief Ibanez:
